CITY OF SAN MATEO
City Council Regular Meeting
May 19, 2025

City Hall Council Chamber
Entrance is on O’Farrell Street

Robert Newsom Jr.
Adam Loraine
Nicole Fernandez

Lisa Diaz Nash
 
AMENDED AGENDA

To join via Zoom – click here: May 19, 2025
To join via telephone:  (408) 638-0968

The City Council meeting will conclude by 11:00 p.m. unless otherwise extended by council vote. 
Any unheard items will automatically move forward to the next regular meeting.

All matters listed under the Consent Calendar are considered by the Council to be routine and will be enacted by one motion without

5.
City Council Meeting Minutes – Approval
Approve the minutes of the City Council meetings as follows: the special and regular meetings held on April 7,
2025, and April 21, 2025; and the special meetings held on April 17, 2025, and April 24, 2025.

CEQA: This minutes approval is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative
activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section
15378(b)(5).)
6.
LGBTQIA+ Progress Pride Flag Display at City Hall – Adoption
Adopt a Resolution to direct that the LGBTQIA+ Progress Pride Flag be flown in recognition of Pride Month
Pursuant to the City's Flag Policy beginning June 1, 2025, and continuing through June 30, 2025.
CEQA: This proposed Resolution is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative
activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section
15378(b)(5).)
7.
29 Baytree Way and 22 De Sabla Road – Final Parcel Map Approval
Adopt a Resolution to approve the final parcel map for a condominium conversion located at 29 Baytree Way and
22 De Sabla Road in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that
will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
8.
Metropolitan Transportation Commission Transit-Oriented Communities Policy Grant – Adoption
Adopt a Resolution committing to completing the City of San Mateo’s tasks toward achieving compliance with the
Metropolitan Transportation Commission’s (MTC) Transit-Oriented Communities (TOC) Policy, as a condition for
MTC to allocate regional discretionary funding to the Housing Policy Development Project (Grand Nexus Study).
CEQA: This Resolution is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity
that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)
(5).)
9.
Fleet Maintenance Services – Agreement Approval
Adopt a Resolution approving an alternative purchasing procedure to award a two-year agreement to Vector
Fleet Management, LLC, for Fleet Maintenance Services in the amount of $2,261,226.42, with three one-year
extensions subject to future Council approval; establish an annual contingency in the amount of $75,000 per
agreement year; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form
presented and issue amendments within the contingency amount.
CEQA: Approval of this agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that
there is no possibility that fleet maintenance services may have a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA
Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)
10.
Wastewater Treatment Plant, Digester 2 Coating Project – Agreement Approval
Approve an Agreement with Brand Safway to conduct Wastewater Treatment Plant Digester 2 Coatings in an
amount not to exceed $406,881.35; approve a contingency of $82,000.00; and authorize the Public Works
Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and approve any necessary change orders
within the approved contingency amount.
CEQA: This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA
Guidelines Section 15301.)
2 of 351

--- page 3 ---
11.
East San Mateo Sanitary Sewer Lift Station Rehabilitation Project – Amendment
Approve Amendment No. 6 with Schaaf & Wheeler for professional design services for the East San Mateo
Sanitary Sewer Lift Station Rehabilitation Project to provide engineering services during construction in an
amount not to exceed $334,247, for a total agreement amount of $2,396,431; amend the Scope of Project;
extend the term; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the amendment in substantially the form
presented and issue amendments within the balance of the previously approved contingency.
CEQA: The work addressed by this administrative report is being undertaken to support the Clean Water Program.
This project is subject to the requirements of the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA), the general
components of which are included as part of the Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR)
(SCH No. 201532006) that was prepared for the Clean Water Program.
12.
On-Call Professional Consultant Services Agreement – Amendment Approval
Approve Amendment No. 3 to the agreement with Sanbell-Bay Area, formerly Bellecci & Associates, for on-call
professional design services increasing the agreement amount by $200,000, for a new agreement total of
$450,000; extending the term of the Agreement to June 30, 2027; and authorizing the Director of Public Works to
execute amendments within the Agreement amount including no-cost extensions.
CEQA: This amendment is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity
that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)
(5).) In addition, the proposed work relating to the Villa Terrace closure and median improvements at East
Bellevue Avenue will include separate CEQA review documentation prepared for the project.
13.
2025 Annual Investment Policy – Approval
Adopt a Resolution approving the City of San Mateo 2025 Investment Policy and authorizing investments in
United States Treasury obligations, Federal Agency obligations and State and Local Municipal obligations with a
maximum maturity of up to seven years and an aggregate amount not to exceed ten percent of the City’s
investment portfolio at the time of purchase.
CEQA: Approval of the City’s 2025 Investment Policy is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is a government
fiscal activity which does not involve any commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially
significant physical impact on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)
14.
Citywide Curb Painting, AB413 Red zones, Markers, Delineators, and Striping Services – Amendment
Approve Amendment No. 1 to the Agreement with Quality Striping, Inc. for thermoplastic, painting, and marking
services to increase the Agreement amount by $230,000, for a total revised Agreement amount of $320,000;
update the payment rates; extend the term through June 30, 2026; and authorize the Public Works Director to
execute the amendment in substantially the form presented and issue no-cost time extensions.
CEQA: Approval of Amendment No. 1 for thermoplastic, striping, and pavement marking services is categorically
exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, maintenance, permitting,
leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, mechanical equipment, or
topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or former use (CEQA Guidelines Section
15301.)
15.
2000 South Delaware Affordable Housing Development – Agreements
Approve the subordination of specified sections of the City Regulatory Agreement with MP Delaware LLC for the
2000 South Delaware Affordable Housing Development to the Deed of Trust of the senior lender, Housing Trust
Silicon Valley, and authorize the City Manager to execute a Subordination Agreement and other agreements

associated with this transaction that do not differ from the term sheet approved by the City Council on August
19, 2024.
CEQA: This agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause
a physical change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
16.
Investment Advisory Services – Agreement
Approve an agreement with Chandler Asset Management for Investment Advisory Services and authorize the
Finance Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: Approval of this Agreement for investment advisory services is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is a
government fiscal activity which does not involve any commitment to any specific project which may result in a
potentially significant physical impact on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)
PUBLIC COMMENT
Members of the public wishing to comment on any item not appearing on the agenda may address the City Council at this time. State
law prevents Council from taking action on any matter not on the agenda; your comments may be referred to staff for follow up.
Public comment is limited to a total of 15 minutes; however, an opportunity for additional public comment may be provided later in
the agenda.
 
PUBLIC HEARING
City Council action on the following public hearing(s) represents a final decision concluding all administrative proceedings. Judicial
review may be had only if a petition is filed with the Court not later than the 90th day following the date the decision is made.
Judicial review of environmental determinations may be subject to a time period for litigation as short as 30 days following the date
the decision is made.
 
17.
Downtown Business Improvement Area – Annual Renewal
Adopt a Resolution to Levy the Annual Assessments for the Downtown Business Improvement Area for fiscal year
2025-26.
CEQA: This item is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will
not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
18.
2025-26 Community Development Block Grant Annual Action Plan – Adoption
Adopt the 2025-26 Community Development Block Grant (CDBG) Annual Action Plan and direct staff to submit
the plan to the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD); authorize the City Manager to
execute the Funding Agreement with HUD for CDBG funds.
CEQA: This plan is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a
physical change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065)
NEW BUSINESS

City Manager, City Attorney and Council Members report on their various assignments and liaison roles and Council requests for

ADJOURNMENT
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
AGENDAS: Agendas and material are posted on the City’s website on the Friday preceding each Council Meeting and can be viewed on the City's
website at www.cityofsanmateo.org . Any supplemental material distributed to the Council after the posting of the agenda will be made part of the
official record.
WATCHING A MEETING ON TV: City Council meetings are broadcast live on Comcast/channel 27, Wave/channel 26, or AT&T/channel 99.
For transmission problems during the broadcast, please call (650) 522-7099. For all other broadcast comments, call (650) 522-7040, Monday-Friday,
8 a.m. - 5 p.m.
WATCHING A MEETING ON A COMPUTER: There are three ways to stream.
1) Public Meeting Portal www.cityofsanmateo.org/publicmeetings
2) City YouTube channel and stream it on YouTube: http://youtube.com/CityofSanMateo
3) Watch TV live stream: https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/193/Channel-San-Mateo-Live-Stream 
PUBLIC COMMENTS/REQUEST TO SPEAK
Prior to the Meeting 
Send comments to: clerk@cityofsanmateo.org until 4 p.m. the day of the meeting.
During the meeting
By Zoom: Click the link at the top of the agenda and you’ll be added to the meeting. All attendees are muted by default. When the item of interest is
open for consideration, select the “Raise Your Hand” icon and you will be called on at the appropriate time.
By telephone: Call (408) 638-0968 and enter the conference ID found at the top of the meeting agenda. When the item of interest is open for
consideration, select *9 to raise your hand. When called upon, press *6 to unmute, state your name and provide your comments.
In Person: At the meeting complete a “Request to Speak” form, submit a request at the speaker kiosk or scan the QR code.
ACCESSIBILITY: In compliance with the Americans with Disabilities Act, those with disabilities requiring special accommodations to participate in this
meeting may contact the City Clerk’s Office at (650) 522-7040 or clerk@cityofsanmateo.org . Notification 48 hours prior to the meeting will enable
the City to make reasonable arrangements to ensure accessibility to this meeting.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
Special Meeting Minutes
City Council
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
 
April 7, 2025
City Hall Council Chambers 5:30 PM
Special Meeting
 
CALL TO ORDER at 5:30 p.m.
Roll Call
Present:
Mayor Newsom, Deputy Mayor Loraine, Council Members: Fernandez, Cwirko-Godycki, and Diaz Nash
AB 2449 Requests and Considerations for Meeting Participation by Teleconference due to Just Cause or Emergency 
Circumstances – there were no requests. 
STUDY SESSION
1.
US 101 / SR 92 Direct Connector — Update
Carolyn Mamaradlo and Amy Linehan, San Mateo County Transportation Authority, gave the presentation and 
status update about the US-101/SR-92 Direct Connector project.
Public Comment:
Organized presentation by Mike Swire stated they oppose this project. Eugene Johnson, Rick Sakuda, Laura Wood, 
Jim Jensen, Kevin Simpson, Olivia McNally, Michael Lim, Laurie Watanuki, Mareva Godfrey, Robert Whitehair, Anna 
Kuhre, Christina Herlitz, Michael Ragan, Peter Mandle, Sheri Boles, Pete Moncheck, Seema Patel, Tom Lease, 
Giselle Godoy, Elaine Salinger, Karen Cutler, Vikash, Nikki Huth, James Cutler, Andrew Lamond, Victoria Tung, 
Susan Manheimer, Eddylee Alvarado, Stu Bruns, Giuliano Carlini, Abibat Rahman-Davies, Jordan Grimes, Annie 
Tsai, Melina Norton, Taso Zografos, and Laurie Hietter spoke in opposed to this project.
Council consensus was for Mayor Newsom and Council Member Cwirko-Godyki to co-author a letter of opposition 
to the San Mateo County Transportation Authority, City/County Association of Governments, Caltrans, Assembly 
Member Papan, and Senator Becker on the project; and invite the City of Foster City to join the letter. Council 
Member Fernandez asked for letter to C/CAG and asked Council Member Diaz Nash to convey as liaison in which 
she agreed.
ADJOURNMENT –The meeting adjourned at 7:10 p.m.
APPROVED BY:                                                        
SUBMITTED BY:
Rob Newsom, Jr., Mayor                      
Martin McTaggart, City Clerk

4.
City Council Meeting Minutes – Approval
Approve the special and regular minutes of the City Council meetings of February 18, 2025, March 3, 2025, and 
March 17, 2025. Approve the minutes of the City Council special meetings of February 22, 2025, March 10, 2025, 
and March 14, 2025.
5.
Boards and Commissions – Establish Annual Appointment Subcommittees
Establish Appointment Subcommittees with Mayor Rob Newsom and the Commission Liaison to interview for 
vacancies on the Community Relations Commission, Library Board, Park and Recreation Commission, Personnel 
Board, Planning Commission, Senior Advisory Commission, Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission, and 
Measure S Oversight Committee. Direct staff, as necessary, if Council Members wish to serve on additional 
Appointment Subcommittees.

6.
Zoning Code Amendments to Implement General Plan Ballot Measure T – Ordinance Adoptions
Adopt two Ordinances that amend the San Mateo Municipal Code Title 27, Zoning. to: 1) implement various 
programs and policies established in San Mateo’s 2023-2031 Housing Element, and 2) implement General Plan 2040 
Ballot Measure T, approved by voters on November 5, 2024; and find that the Ordinances are exempt from further 
environmental review pursuant to California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) Section 15183 (Projects Consistent 
With a Community Plan, General Plan, or Zoning).
Enactment:  Ordinance Nos. 2025-03 and 2025-04
7.
Peninsula Heights North Phase, 2800, and 2988 Campus Drive – Agreement
Adopt a Resolution to approve the final map and the subdivision improvement agreement for the Peninsula Heights 
North Phase subdivision located at 2800 and 2988 Campus Drive and authorize the Public Works Director to 
execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
Enactment:  Resolution No. 29 (2025)
8.
E 41st Place & Pacific Boulevard Trash Capture Project – Agreement
Approve an agreement with GSW Construction, Inc. for the E 41st Place and Pacific Boulevard Trash Capture project 
in the amount of $257,240; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $51,400; and authorize the Public 
Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change orders as allowed 
by the contract documents and within the contingency amount.
9.
On-Site Fueling Station Replacement and Canopy Addition – Purchase and Construction Contracts
Adopt a Resolution approving an alternative purchasing procedure for a purchase contract with Petroleum 
Marketing Equipment for fueling equipment and a tank for the On-Site Fueling Station Replacement and Canopy 
Addition Project in the amount of $125,606.39, and establish a contingency reserve of $13,000 for the purchase 
contract; approve a construction contract with Armer Norman & Associates, Inc. in the amount of $978,988.00, and 
establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $150,000.00; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute 
the purchase contract and construction contract in substantially the forms presented and issue change orders as 
allowed by the contract documents and within the contingency reserves.
Enactment:  Resolution No. 30 (2025)
10.
Citywide Small Trash Capture Project – Contingency Reserve Increase
Approve a contingency reserve increase in the amount of $325,000 for the construction agreement with United 
Storm Water, Inc. for the Citywide Small Trash Capture Project, revising the original contingency reserve from 
$105,000 to $430,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to issue change orders within the contingency 
amount.
11.
Marina Lagoon Vegetation and Water Quality Management — Agreement
Approve a three-year agreement with Waterworks Industries, Inc. for Marina Lagoon Vegetation and Water Quality 
Management in the amount of $1,552,009, with two one-year options to extend, for a total potential amount not 
to exceed $2,662,963; approve a contingency reserve in the amount of $80,000; and authorize the Public Works 
Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented, to execute each optional one-year 
extension to the agreement, and sign change orders within the contingency reserve.
12.
Gateway Park Pedestrian Bridge Replacement Project – Bid Rejection
Adopt a Resolution to reject all bids received for the Gateway Park Pedestrian Bridge Replacement Project.
Enactment:  Resolution No. 31 (2025)

13.
Enterprise Resource Planning Support Service – Agreement
Approve a new Statement of Work to the master services agreement with Collaborative Solutions, LLC for 
Enterprise Resource Planning Support Service (ERP) post-production support services in the amount of $242,000 
and authorize the City Manager to approve the Statement of Work in substantially the form presented.
14.
Temporary Standby Generator for Dale Avenue Pump Station Upgrade – Contract Change Order
Approve Contract Change Order No. 8 to the Agreement with Herc Rentals, Inc. for a temporary emergency standby 
generator to support the Dale Ave Pump Station Upgrade project in an amount not to exceed $66,944.28, 
increasing the total agreement amount to $781,731.99; increase the contingency reserve by $22,350; extend the 
Agreement term to April 30, 2025; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the change order in 
substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the contingency amount.
15.
Consulting Recruitment Services – Change Order
Approve Change Order No. 1 to the agreement with It's Personnel Consulting for the purpose of professional 
recruitment services in the amount of $100,000.00 for a new agreement total of $150,000.00; and authorize the 
City Manager to execute the Change Order in substantially the form presented.
16.
Mobile Parking Revenue Collection – Amendment
Approve Amendment No. 1 to the agreement with PayByPhone US, Inc. for mobile parking payment services in the 
amount of $65,000 for a new agreement total of $150,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the 
amendment in substantially the form presented.
17.
San Mateo Public Library Foundation Operating Lease – Amendment
Approve an Amendment to the Property Lease and Operating Agreement with the San Mateo Public Library 
Foundation to extend the lease for an additional year commencing retroactively on April 1, 2025, through March 
31, 2026; and authorize its execution by the City Librarian.
18.
SEIU Local 521, Maintenance, Side Letter of Agreement Regarding Salary Increase – Adoption
Adopt a Resolution to amend the SEIU Local 521, Maintenance Memorandum of Understanding to implement 
additional equity salary adjustments.
Enactment:  Resolution No. 32 (2025)
19.
San Mateo Management Employees’ Association – Memorandum of Understanding Amendments
Adopt a Resolution to amend the Memorandum of Understanding (“MOU”) between the City of San Mateo (“City”) 
and the San Mateo Management Employees’ Association (“SMMEA”) for a term through April 22, 2028.
Enactment:  Resolution No. 33 (2025)
PUBLIC COMMENT
Trina Pierce, President of North Central Neighborhood Association, and Judy Hendrix stated they and the residents want 
their parking spaces back instead of the bike lanes. Olivia McNally, Shoreview/Parkside Neighborhood President, would 
like a recreation room on the eastside to be able to hold community meetings/events. She also stated that she has 
requested multiple times to have a speed assessment done in the Parkside area especially near Parkside Elementary 
School for safety reasons.

PUBLIC HEARING
20.
Fiscal Year 2025-26 Comprehensive Fee Schedule — Approval
Karley Toffey, Senior Management Analyst, and Karen Huang, Finance Director, gave the presentation.
Public Comment – there were no speakers.
Council asked questions and made comments.
Motion to approve waiver of park and rec facility, non-profits or neighborhood associations. Park and Recreation 
Director will create a policy, this is a stopgap measure.
Motion to Adopt a Resolution to approve the revisions to the proposed fiscal year 2025-26 Comprehensive Fee 
Schedule. Motion passed 5-0.
Moved:
Cwirko-Godycki, Seconded: Fernandez
Ayes: 
Newsom, Loraine, Fernandez, Cwirko-Godycki, and Diaz Nash
Noes: 
None
Enactment:  Resolution No. 34 (2025)
21.
Status of Vacancies and Recruitment and Retention Efforts (Assembly Bill 2561/Government Code 3502.3) – Public 
Hearing
Conduct a Public Hearing in accordance with Government Code Section 3502.3 (Assembly Bill 2561) to present the 
status of vacancies, recruitment, and retentions efforts in advance of the adoption of an annual budget.
Aracelia Esparza, Director of Human Resources, gave a presentation.
Jesse Dolan, representing SEIU, gave a presentation.
Council asked questions and made comments.
Director of Human Resources Esparza, and Jesse Dolan, representing SEIU, responded.
The Mayor opened public comment.
Public Comment – Julie Lind, San Mateo Labor Council representing 103 affiliate unions and over 95,000 workers 
and their families countywide, spoke about the pressing need to support our city employees.
Council recessed from 9:00 p.m. to 9:10 p.m.
NEW BUSINESS
22.
General Fund Reserve Policy – Review
Karen Huang, Finance Director, gave the presentation on the General Fund Reserve Policy and potential 
modifications.
Public Comment – there were no speakers.
Support from Council on proposed suggestions from staff. Unanimous approval of Council.

REPORTS AND ANNOUNCEMENTS
City Manager, City Attorney and Council Members reported on their various assignments and liaison roles and noted past 
and future events. 
Danielle Cwirko-Godycki proposed that the City introduce a “Mayoral Minute”, as a once per month outreach effort on 
the City’s social meeting. Monthly update in newsletter.  Majority of Council approved it. 
Public Works Director Matt Fabry gave an update on the train quiet zone progress.
Council convened to Closed Session at 10:00 p.m.
CLOSED SESSION
23.

(Paragraph (1) of subdivision (d) of Section 54956.9)

AB 2449 Requests and Considerations for Meeting Participation by Teleconference due to Just Cause or Emergency

STUDY SESSION
1.
General Fund 2025-26 Operating Budget – Preview
Karen Huang, Finance Director, gave a presentation on the General Fund 2024-25 operating budget preview.
Public Comment: Mason Fong offered suggestions for enhancing the City’s financial strategies. He recommended 
exploring the potential for generating revenue by selling water from the Water Treatment Plant to Cal Water. He 
also expressed concern about the City’s 25% reserve policy, suggesting it could be adjusted to 15% to free up funds 
for other priorities. Mr. Fong advocated for renovating the Third Avenue Garage sooner rather than delaying the 
project, noting that construction costs will likely increase over time. He referenced Sunnyvale as a city with policies 
worth considering and encouraged the City to prioritize projects that have the potential to generate revenue. 
Council asked questions and made comments. 
Staff to come back with information, bring something back in June for Community Budget.
2.
2025-30 Capital Improvement Program Plan Preview
Matt Fabry, Public Works Director, and Joanne Magrini, Park and Recreation Director, gave the presentation on the 
2025-30 Capital Improvement Plan.
Public Comment: Mason Fong suggested a framework for prioritizing City projects. First, he recommended 
evaluating projects based on the long-term cost of deferred maintenance and their potential to generate revenue 
for the City. Second, he proposed exploring opportunities to recapture use tax revenue—for example, by making it 
a conditional use to redirect sales tax funds from the County to the City to support construction efforts. Third, he 
encouraged the City to consider a thought exercise of using reserves to help fund currently unfunded projects.
Council asked questions and made comments.

10.
Housing Element Implementation – Anti-Displacement and Tenant Protection Policies
Rachel Horst, Housing & Neighborhood Services Manager, and Jennifer Mora, Housing Specialist, gave the 
presentation on how to implement the tenant protection/anti-displacement policies in the 2023-2031 Housing 
Element.
Public Comment
Rhovy Lyn Antonio, Mitch Speigle, Michael Johnston, Tom Blake, Jeff LaMont, Desiree Tang, Marina van 
Blommestein, Laurie Watanuki, Brian Ponty, Mark Rain, Frank Vella, Gary Isoardi, Don Peterson, Martin Elliott, 
Fred Efltkei, Shawn Fahrenbruch, Brendon Aiello, Mason Fong, Alane Gilbrech, Chris Eckert, Colleen White, Amelia 
Mendez, John Mendez, Karim Sarrat, Jen Kilroy, Tina Wong, Michael Ragan Paul K., Jonathan Stone, and Gina 
Papan spoke in opposition to expanded tenant protections, such as rental registry, increased relocation assistance 
and other mechanisms due to undue burden to housing providers, disincentives for small business owners to enter 
the rental marked and increase constraints for landlords.
Bill Newell, John Medina, Teresa Gebler, Tina Doede, Rev. Penny Nixon, Seema Patel, John Love, Rosa Maria 
Fonseca, Imeldia Navarro, Lauren Matthews, Jorge Vergam, Ricardo Saucedo, Robert Whitehair, Terri Whitehair, 
John Ebneter, Alexis Lewis, Rev Alvaro Duran, Laura Hinz, Jessica Vacketta, Chris Worthmann, Paola Arellana 
Rasalas, Ted McKinnon, Reina, Rick Bonilla, Karyl Eldgridge, Stephanie Reyes, Amanda Chang, Suzanne Moore, 
Krista Hanson spoke in support of protections for tenants such as rental registry, emergency rental assistance, 
prohibition of no fault eviction, right of return after remodels, and increase relocation assistance.

--- page 19 ---
City Council Regular Meeting Minutes – 4/21/2025
Page 4
Council recessed from 9:32 p.m. to 9:42 p.m.
Council asked further questions of staff and deliberated. 
Question #1. Given the commitment in Policy H.3.4(a) to extending relocation assistance for no-fault evictions for 
those with tenure less than one-year (day one, 3, 6, 9, 11 months)? If so how many months of assistance? –
 
Council consensus was for 11 months, with 1 month of relocation assistance.
 
Question #2. Would the City Council like to pursue a policy related to right-to-return as described in Policy H.3.4(b)?
 
Council consensus directed staff to notify tenant first of new market rate unit.
 
Question #3. Given the commitment in Policy H.3.4(c) to strengthening the enforcement penalty structure of the 
City’s existing ordinance on relocation assistance for tenants displaced by code enforcement activities, does the City 
Council wish to move forward with changing the existing requirement (3 months of HUD FMR) to actual 3 months’ 
rent (or costs)?
Council unanimously supports. Staff directed to propose ordinance amendments that align with best practices from 
comparable cities.
Council called for vote to continue the meeting after 11:00 p.m. Motion passed 5-0.
Ayes: 
Newsom, Loraine, Fernandez, Cwirko-Godycki, and Diaz Nash
Noes: 
None
Question #4. Would the City Council like to pursue a rent registry, pursue a different model for data tracking, or 
rely on existing data sources to achieve the goals of Policy H.3.6?
 
Council consensus was to not pursue this but to review in a year and to return to City Council with other options 
for data tracking.
 
Question #5. Are there other policy alternatives the City Council would like to pursue based on the findings in this 
report (emergency rental assistance funding and program)?
 
Council unanimously indicated yes for emergency rental assistance.
 
Question #6. Does the City Council wish to prioritize any of these items as staff continues with implementation?  
Council did not formally rank the items, but indicated that enforcement (Q3), right-to-return (Q2), and relocation 
assistance (Q1) were higher priorities for near-term action. Rental registry (Q4) was identified as needing further 
analysis before moving forward.
11.
City Council Priority List – Adoption
This item was moved to the May 5, 2025 regular meeting due to the length of this meeting.
REPORTS AND ANNOUNCEMENTS
City Manager, City Attorney and Council Members reported on their various assignments and liaison roles and noted past 
and future events, along with updates.
ADJOURNMENT –The meeting adjourned at 11:30 p.m.

May 19, 2025 
SUBJECT:
LGBTQIA+ Progress Pride Flag Display at City Hall – Adoption 
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to direct that the LGBTQIA+ Progress Pride Flag be flown in recognition of Pride Month Pursuant to the 
City's Flag Policy beginning June 1, 2025, and continuing through June 30, 2025.
BACKGROUND:
On June 3, 2014, the San Mateo County Board of Supervisors unanimously adopted a resolution establishing the Lesbian, 
Gay, Bisexual, Transgender, Queer, Intersex, and Asexual (LGBTQIA+) Commission, the first county or city-level commission 
in California dedicated to addressing the needs of the LGBTQIA+ community. The Commission’s mission is to cultivate San 
Mateo County as a welcoming, affirming, and safe environment where its lesbian, gay, bisexual, transgender, queer, 
intersex, asexual, and gender expansive community members can thrive.
In 2020, the Commission launched its Pride Month Visibility Campaign, encouraging all cities and communities in San 
Mateo County to recognize and support Pride Month each June. Since 2021, all 20 cities within the county, including the 
City of San Mateo, have participated by issuing proclamations and raising the Pride Flag.
To continue the City’s commitment to promoting diversity and inclusion, staff recommends that the City Council adopt the 
attached Resolution authorizing the display of the LGBTQIA+ Progress Pride Flag during the month of June, in accordance 
with the City Hall Flag Display Policy.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budgetary impact associated with the adoption of the attached Resolution.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This proposed Resolution is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will 
not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS
Att 1 – Proposed Resolution

CITY OF SAN MATEO
RESOLUTION NO. ____ 2025
DIRECTION THAT THE LGBTQIA+ PROGRESS PRIDE FLAG BE FLOWN FROM JUNE 1, 2025 THROUGH JUNE 30, 
2025 IN RECOGNITION OF PRIDE MONTH PURSUANT TO THE CITY OF SAN MATEO’S FLAG POLICY
WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo’s Flag Policy directs that the Flag of the United States of America 
together with the Flag of the State of California shall be displayed on exterior flag poles at major City facilities, 
including the flagpole at City Hall; and
WHEREAS, the City’s flagpoles are not intended to serve as a forum of free expression by the public; and
WHEREAS,  flags other than the Flag of the United States of America, the Flag of the State of California 
or other governmental flag shall only be displayed upon approval by the City Council of the City of San Mateo by 
adoption of a resolution; and
WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo adopted the Flag Policy on September 3, 2024; and
WHEREAS, in 2020, the San Mateo County LGBTQIA+ Commission initiated a Pride Month Visibility 
Campaign and invited all twenty (20) cities in San Mateo County to raise the Pride Flag in the month of June.
WHEREAS, in 2025, the City Council wishes to express its support for the LGBTQIA+ community and join 
the County of San Mateo to observe Pride Month with raising of a Progress Pride Flag to honor the history of the 
LGBTQIA+ movement and to support the rights of all citizens to experience equality and freedom from 
discrimination. 
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY RESOLVES 
that: 
1.
The City Council hereby directs that the LGBTQIA+ Progress Pride Flag be flown beginning June 1, 
2025 and continuing through June 30, 2025 on the exterior flagpole at City Hall in addition to the 
regularly flown flags pursuant to the City’s Flag Policy.

SUBJECT:
29 Baytree Way and 22 De Sabla Road – Final Parcel Map Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve the final parcel map for a condominium conversion located at 29 Baytree Way and 22 De 
Sabla Road in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
On October 10, 2023, the Planning Commission approved the tentative parcel map for the conversion of an existing 
residential duplex to two (2) residential condominiums at 29 Baytree Way & 22 De Sabla Road (Planning Application # PA-
2022-064). In accordance with San Mateo Municipal Code (SMMC) Section 26.65.020, maps for conversions to 
condominiums are subject to subdivision map review by the City (SMMC Section 26.52), regardless of the number of lots 
or condominiums. Therefore, the final parcel map is subject to SMMC Section 26.52.090 and City Council approval is 
required prior to being recorded.
In January 2024, the Subdivider filed Parcel Map No. 483 with the City for condominium purposes in compliance with the 
Conditions of Approval (COAs), the Subdivision Map Act, and SMMC Section 26. The final parcel map was reviewed for 
accuracy and completeness by the City’s survey and mapping consultant, CSG Consultants. A copy of the final parcel map is 
included as Attachment 2. 
Pursuant to SMMC Section 26.52.070(4), 26.65.060(7), and the COAs, all required public improvements, including 
sidewalk, curb, and gutter replacement on De Sabla Road, were completed and the encroachment permit was finalized on 
October 7, 2024. Consistent with SMMC Section 26.65.060(3) & (4) and the COAs, the building permit improvements were 
completed, and the building permit was finalized on March 7, 2025. All the conditions required for final parcel map 
approval have been satisfied. 
The covenants, conditions, and restrictions (CC&Rs) for this project have been reviewed by the City Attorney's Office, 
Public Works Department, and Planning Division. The CC&Rs will be recorded with the County Recorder’s Office prior to 
the sale of the condominiums (included as Attachment #3). 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Approval of the final parcel map will have no budgetary impact.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

CONDOMINIUM DECLARATION OF COVENANTS, CONDITIONS AND RESTRICTIONS
FOR BAYTREE WAY CONDOMINIUMS

THIS DECLARATION, made on the date hereinafter set forth, by ROBERT LORENZEN,
JULIENNE LORENZEN, ADRIENNE RUSSELL, ROBERT RUSSELL, KIRK SYME and KATHERINE
SYME, hereinafter collectively referred to as "Declarant," is made with reference to the following facts:

A. Location of Property. Declarant is the owner of that certain real property (the
"Property") located in the City of San Mateo ("City"), State of California, more particularly described
as Parcel A of Parcel Map No. 483 filed for record in the Official Records of the County of San
Mateo, State of California, as Document No. 20__- -0O0, Book ___ of
Condominium Maps, Pages __-

B. Intention. The Property is improved with buildings consisting of two (2) residential
units that Declarant intends to subdivide into two (2) Condominiums consisting of separate interests in
the two Units, and undivided interests in the remaining property.

C. Owners’ Interests. The development shall be referred to as the "Project" as defined in
Section 1.28. Each Condominium Unit in the Project shall consist of a three dimensional space and
all improvements therein, and an interest in the Common Area as shown on the Condominium Plan,
and defined in this Declaration.

D. General Plan of Improvement. Declarant intends by this document to impose upon the
Project mutually beneficial restrictions under a general plan of improvement for the benefit of all of the
Condominiums and the Owners thereof.

NOW, THEREFORE, Declarant hereby declares that the Project shall be held, conveyed, mortgaged,
encumbered, leased, rented, used, occupied, sold, and improved, subject to the following declarations,
limitations, covenants, conditions, restrictions and easements, all of which are imposed as equitable
servitudes pursuant to a general plan for the development of the Project for the purpose of enhancing
and protecting the value and attractiveness of the Project, and every part of the Project, in accordance
with the plan for the improvements of the Project and the division of the Project into Condominiums.
All of the limitations, covenants, conditions, restrictions and easements shall constitute covenants which
shall run with the land and shall be binding upon Declarant and its successors and assigns, and all
parties having or acquiring any right, title or interest in or to any part of the Project or the property
which constitutes the Project.

ARTICLE |. DEFINITIONS

1.1. | "Assessment": That portion of the cost of maintaining, improving, repairing, operating
and managing the Project which is to be paid by each Owner as determined by the Association, and
shall include regular and special Assessments.

1.2. "Association": The BAYTREE WAY ASSOCIATION, an unincorporated association, the
Members of which shall be the two (2) Owners of Condominiums in the Project.

1.3. "Building": A building in which a Unit is located, as described on the Condominium
Plan.

1.4. "City": The City of San Mateo, California.
1.5. "Common Area": All of the Project except the Units, and includes all of Parcel A as

shown on the Map with the exception of the Units. Title to the Common Area shall be held in
undivided interests as provided in the Condominium Plan by all of the Owners as tenants-in-common.

1.6. "Common Expenses": The actual and estimated expenses of operating the Common
Area and any reasonable reserve for such purposes as found and determined by the Members and all
sums designated Common Expenses by or pursuant to the Declaration.

1.7. "Common Interest": The proportionate undivided interest in the Common Area that is
part of each Condominium as set forth in this Declaration.

1.8. "Condominium": An estate in real property as defined in California Civil Code §§783
and 4125(b), consisting of an undivided interest in common in a portion of the Project and a separate
interest in space called a Unit.

1.9. "Condominium Plan": The recorded three-dimensional plan of the Condominiums built

or to be built on the Project which identifies the Common Area and each separate interest pursuant to

by reference herein.
1.10. "County": The County of San Mateo.

1.11. "Declarant": ROBERT LORENZEN, JULIENNE LORENZEN, ADRIENNE RUSSELL,
ROBERT RUSSELL, KIRK SYME and KATHERINE SYME, or any successor or assign that expressly
assumes the rights and duties of the Declarant(s) hereunder, in a recorded written document.

1.12. "Declaration": This Declaration, as amended or supplemented from time to time.
1.13. "Eligible Mortgages": Mortgages held by "Eligible Mortgage Holders”.

1.14. "Eligible Mortgage Holder": A First Lender who has requested notice of certain
matters from the Association in accordance with Section 9.6.

1.15. "Eligible Insurer or Guarantor": An insurer or governmental guarantor of a First
Mortgage who has requested notice of certain matters from the Association in accordance with
Section 9.6.C.

1.16. "Exclusive Use Common Area": Those portions of the Common Area set aside for
exclusive use of an Owner pursuant to Section 2.2.C, which shall constitute "Exclusive Use Common
Area" within the meaning of California Civil Code section 4145.

1.17. "First Lender": Any person, entity, bank, savings and loan association, insurance
company, or financial institution holding a recorded First Mortgage on any Condominium.

1.18. "First Mortgage": Any recorded mortgage made in good faith and for value on a
Condominium with first priority over other mortgages thereon.

1.19. "Foreclosure": The legal process by which the mortgaged property of a borrower in
default under a mortgage is sold, and the borrower's interest in such property is sold, pursuant to
California Civil Code § 2924a et seq. or sale by the Court pursuant to California Code of Civil
Procedure § 725a et seq. and any other applicable law.

1.20. "Map": That Parcel Map described above in Introductory Paragraph A.

1.21. "Member": A person entitled to membership in the Association as provided herein.

1.22. "Mortgage": A deed of trust as well as a mortgage.

1.23. "Mortgagee": A beneficiary or a holder of a deed of trust as well as a mortgagee.

ARTICLE II. DESCRIPTION OF PROJECT, DIVISION OF PROPERTY, AND CREATION OF
PROPERTY RIGHTS

2.1. Description of Project: The Project is a condominium project consisting of the land
which makes up the Project, the Condominiums and all other improvements thereon. The Project
consists of two (2) Condominium Units and the Common Area. Reference is made to the
Condominium Plan for further details.

2.2. __ Division of Property: The Project is divided as follows:

A. Units: Each of the Units is shown, numbered and designated in the
Condominium Plan designated by the words “Unit” followed by the designation 1 or 2, and consists of
the space described on the Condominium Plan as the Unit. Each Unit includes the utility installations
located within its boundaries as to which the Owner has the exclusive use. Each Unit includes both
the portions of the Building as so described and the airspace and land so encompassed within the Unit
boundaries. The Unit does not include those areas and those things which are defined as "Common
Area” in Section 1.5. Each Unit shall have appurtenant to it nonexclusive rights for ingress, egress and
support through the Common Area.

B. Common Area: The remainder of the Project constitutes "Common Area" as
defined in Section 1.5. Each Condominium Owner shall have, as appurtenant to his or her Unit, an
undivided interest in the Common Area, as provided in the Condominium Plan attached as Exhibit “A”,
subject to the rights of each Owner in the Common Area. Each Condominium includes a Unit and
such undivided interest in the Common Area. The Common Interest appurtenant to each Unit is
permanent in character and cannot be altered without the unanimous consent of the Owners and of the
holders of first mortgages on the Condominiums, as expressed in an amended Declaration. The
undivided Common Interest cannot be separated from the Unit, and any conveyance or transfer of the

04/02/25 3
T:\WPWIN60\PROJECTS\BAYTREE WA Y\DECLARATION[04 02 25].doc

38 of 351


--- page 39 ---
Unit shall include the undivided Common Interest, the Owner's membership in the Association, and any
other benefits or burdens appurtenant to that Owner's Condominium. Each Owner may use the
Common Area in accordance with the purposes for which it is intended subject to this Declaration and
the Rules, without hindering the exercise of or encroaching upon the rights of any other Owners.

C. Exclusive Use Common Area: The following described portions of the
Common Area referred to as Exclusive Use Common Area are set aside and allocated for the
exclusive use of the Owner of the Condominium to which they are attached or assigned as shown on
the Condominium Plan and are appurtenant to that Condominium:

(1) Rear yard area designated “RY-1” and “RY-2’. Easements for the
exclusive use of said areas shall be granted as appurtenances to the correspondingly numbered Units.

(2) Parcels designated “EUCA-1” and “EUCA-2” are Exclusive Use Common
Areas appurtenant to the correspondingly numbered Units.

2.3. Rights of Entry and Use: The Units and Common Area shall be subject to the
following rights of entry and use:

A. The access rights of the Association as described in Section 5.2.B to maintain,
repair or replace improvements or property located in the Common Area, that are exterior of the Units.

B. The rights of the Association or the Owners to install, maintain, repair or
replace utilities as described in Article VI.

C. The encroachment rights described in Section 9.5.

D. The rights of Owners to make improvements or alterations authorized by

California Civil Code § 4760, subject to the provisions of Section 7.8.

2.4. Partition Prohibited: The Common Area shall remain undivided as set forth above.
Except as provided by California Civil Code §4610 or authorized under Section 8.2B, no Owner shall
bring any action for partition of the Common Area, it being agreed that this restriction is necessary in
order to preserve the rights of the Owners with respect to the operation and management of the
Project. Judicial partition by sale of a single Condominium owned by two (2) or more persons and
division of the sale proceeds is not prohibited by this paragraph.

2.5. All Easements Part of Common Plan: Whenever any easements are reserved or
created or are to be reserved or created in this Declaration, such easements shall constitute equitable
servitudes for the mutual benefit of all property in the Project, even if only certain Units are specifically
mentioned as subject to or benefiting from a particular easement. Easements referred to in this
Declaration that are created by grant deeds, subsequent to the date of this Declaration shall be part of
the common plan created by this Declaration for the benefit of all property Owners within the Project.

2.6. Party Walls: As depicted on the Condominium Plan, on Sheets 3, 4 and 6, the
boundary line between the two Units, both vertically and horizontally, is designated “Party Wall.” The
structure within the area so indicated constitutes a “Party Wall.” To the extent not inconsistent with
this Section, the general rules of law regarding Party Walls and liability for property damage due to
negligence or willful acts or omissions shall apply thereto. The cost of reasonable repair and
maintenance of a Party Wall shall be shared by the Owners who make use of the wall in proportion to
such use. If a Party Wall is destroyed or damaged by fire or other casualty, any Owner who has used
the wall may restore it, and if the other Owners thereafter make use of the wall they shall contribute to
the cost of restoration thereof in proportion to such use; provided, however that the Owner or Owners
whose negligent act or omission proximately caused the damage or destruction, shall bear the full cost
of restoration that is not covered by insurance. An Owner who by its negligent or willful act causes
the Party Walls to be exposed to the elements shall bear the whole cost of furnishing the necessary
protection against such elements. The right of any Owner to contribution from any other Owner under
