1.1.2
PERSONNEL LIFTS.  All Personnel Lifts shall be serviced 
and tested by a qualified technician in accordance with manufacturer’s 
recommendation, and state and federal regulations. Annual Aerial and 
dielectric testing standards apply.
1.1.3
POOL CARS. In addition to maintaining the City Pool vehicles according to the standards 
set forth in this agreement, Contractor shall wash, clean and vacuum interior, and fuel all 
pool vehicles weekly.  
1.1.4
CUSTOMER NOTIFICATION.  Contractor shall in conjunction with the Contracting Officer, 
establish notification systems that are responsive to the City Customer’s needs.  The 
system shall provide customers with monthly schedule of vehicles due for service with at 
least 15-days lead time. Additionally, the contractor shall provide a means of real time 
notification of vehicle status to the end user via Heads Up Display accessible to remote 
locations (URL, App, feed etc.) and configurable to specific department assigned vehicles. 
Information should have functionality to automatically scroll to allow for all vehicles to be 
displayed. Display must include provisions for – Department (filterable or multiple 
department specific feeds), city unit number, vehicle year make model, Date & time In, 
Service description, Status, Estimated Completion, location. A typical system may be web 
90 of 351

--- page 91 ---
or app based and must allow for projection to computer monitor / web connected TV, 
interoperability with existing hardware is preferred.
1.1.5 INSPECTIONS AND CERTIFICATIONS.  Contractor shall perform all inspections and obtain any 
required certifications in accordance with local, state and federal law and regulations, these 
include but are not limited to annual speedometer calibration and certification meeting AAA 
or equivalent standards, SMOG, periodic smoke inspection test, dielectric and load testing of 
personnel lifts and any other established by regulation or industry standard.
1.1.5.1 Contractor shall perform all inspections and maintain all required records to 
comply with the California “Biennial Inspection of Terminals (BIT) Program.  Contractor 
shall also perform all other statutory inspections when and as required by Federal or 
State Law.
 
1.1.6 ROAD TESTS.  Contractor shall road test each vehicle and operationally test each piece of 
equipment after completion of a preventive maintenance inspection and/or repair.  
1.1.7 ON-BOARD DATA COLLECTION SYSTEM.  The maintenance levels as set forth in 1.1.1 are 
established as contract a starting point.  The city will install an on-board collection data system to 
all non-emergency fleet vehicles.  The contractor is expected to work with the city to define 
techniques for utilizing the on-board data collection system to improve maintenance techniques 
and reduce costs.  This will be a factor consider in the Key Performance Indicators as described in 
2.13.1.
1.1.8 COMPRESED NATURAL GAS (CNG) VEHILCES.   The contractor is expected to provide 
technicians certified in the repair and inspection of CNG vehicle systems.  However, when such 
repairs and or maintenance cannot be accomplished at city owned facilities the contractor will 
engage outside repair/maintenance services at contractor's expense.

An updated copy must be provided to the Contracting Officer on contract start date and as changes 
occur.
The plan shall include:

areas to be inspected on either a scheduled or unscheduled basis, how often inspections will be 
accomplished, and the title of the individual(s) who will perform the inspection.
1.3.2  The methods for identifying and preventing defects in the quality of service performed 
before the level of performance becomes unacceptable.
1.3.3  On-site records of all inspections conducted by the Contractor and necessary corrective 
action taken.  This documentation shall be entered into the contractor’s Fleet Management

contract.

1.5  PHYSICAL SECURITY.  Contractor shall be responsible for safeguarding all city property provided for 
Contractor use.  At the close of each work period, facilities, equipment, and materials shall be secured.
1.5.1  Key / Access Control Device.  The Contractor shall establish and implement methods of 
insuring that all keys and access control devices issued to the Contractor by the City are not lost 
or misplaced, and are not used by unauthorized persons.  No facility/building keys or access 
devices issued the Contractor by the City shall be duplicated.  
1.5.1.1  The Contractor shall report the occurrences of a lost or duplicated keys or access 
devices to the Contracting Officer.
1.5.1.2  In the event keys, other than master keys are lost or duplicated, the Contractor will be 
required, upon direction of the Contracting Officer, to have new keys made or replace the 
affected lock or locks; however the City at its option, may replace the affected lock or locks or 
have new keys made.  When the replacement of locks or obtaining new keys is performed by 
the City, the total cost of obtaining the keys or the replacement of the lock(s) shall be deducted 
from the monthly payment due the Contractor.  In the event a master key is lost or duplicated, 
all locks and keys for that system shall be replaced by the City and the total cost deducted from 
the monthly payment due.
1.5.1.3  It is the responsibility of the Contractor to prohibit the use of keys and access devices 
issued by the City by any persons other than the Contractor's employees or city employees 
engaged in the performance of assigned work in those areas.

Contractor's responsibilities for emergency support are described in Part IV - Section 6.

SECTION 2
SPECIAL PROVISIONS
2.0 to 2.2 RESERVED
2.3  OTHER CONTRACTS - The City reserves the right to let other contracts in connection with City 
equipment and vehicles as it may deem necessary. The City's right to let other contracts applies to any 
work outside the Scope of Work as described for normal operation and maintenance services.
2.4  INCLUSION/EXCLUSION - The City may add additional units by notifying the Contractor in writing.  
Any unit to be added to the Contract will be included in the class of vehicles which most closely 
resembles the unit as mutually agreed upon by the City and the Contractor.  To be effective, the notice 
adding a unit to the Contract must describe the additional unit by manufacturer, model and serial 
number.  The notice must include fleet number, VIN number, license plate number (where applicable) 
and a brief description of the unit.
2.4.1  Notice of Inclusion to the Contractor will take effect upon the seventh calendar day 
following its receipt and be prorated by the Contractor, or on such later date as specified therein.  
Each unit so added will be subject to this Contract as of the effective date; Contract charges and 
penalties will begin to accrue for units added to the fleet (see unit pricing sheet) at the same rate 
as existing units in its assigned class.
2.4.2  Any unit which is subject to this contract may be excluded from the Contract by means of a 
written notice from the City to the Contractor.  Any such notice takes effect upon its receipt by 
the Contractor unless the notice provides otherwise.  To be effective the notice must describe the 
unit by manufacturer, VIN number, fleet number, and include a brief description of the unit to be 
excluded.  
2.5  VARIATION IN WORKLOAD.
2.5.1  If at the end of each three months of Contractor performance, the number of 
vehicle/equipment in Technical Attachment B varies above or below 8%, negotiations for an 
equitable price adjustment may be initiated by either the City or the Contractor.  Adjustments to 
95 of 351

--- page 96 ---
the contract amount will be made only for that portion of the increase or decrease in excess of 
8%.
2.5.2  The contract amount used as a basis for computing the equitable adjustment will not 
contain any Over and Above amounts.  All Over and Above amounts, either in the basic contract 
price or added by modification will be subtracted from the total contract amount in order to 
determine the adjustable contract amount.
2.5.3  The Contractor will notify the Contracting Officer in writing of all expected work variances 
as described in this change which may result in a request by the Contractor for equitable price 
increase and will provide the estimated amount of such price increases.  Such notices will be 
provided at the earliest practicable time but in no event later than prior to performance of such 
work variances.  The City will have no obligation under this clause unless a modification to this 
contract will have been issued establishing a line item in the schedule to cover such work 
variances.
2.5.4  The technical attachments referred to above and attached hereto will be the basis for all 
variation in workload computations for the duration of this contract including options.  Only the 
elements described above will be the basis for an equitable adjustment based upon workload 
variations.
2.6  CHANGEOVER PERIOD - Upon the award of this Contract, and prior to start-up, there will be a sixty 
(60) day Changeover Period during which the Contractor will phase in.  During the Changeover Period, 
the Contractor will ensure an adequate inventory of parts, lubricants, etc.; the Contractor will take all 
necessary steps and actions to ensure full administration of administrative program, including personnel 
hiring and training, setting up records, and all other procedures required for changeover.  It will be the 
Contractor's responsibility during the Changeover Period to familiarize himself with the total fleet 
operations and requirements of the City covered by this Contract, so that he may be able to schedule 
personnel and maintenance to maximize fleet operations.
2.7  CITY OBSERVATION - City personnel may from time to time observe Contractor's operations.  
However, these personnel may not interfere with Contractor's performance.
2.8  CITY PERFORMANCE OF SERVICES DURING LABOR STRIKES - The services called for under this 
Contract are of critical importance.  In the event of a labor strike by the Contractor's employees, the 
Contractor will be responsible for maintaining the continuity of service to the City.  However, the City 
reserves the right to take over the performance of this Contract.  In such event, the services will be 
performed exclusively by City employees or by another Contractor and not by a mix of City and 
non-striking Contractor's employees.  Under such circumstances and at the direction of the Contracting 
Officer, the Contractor agrees to remove its non-striking work force from performance sites and not to 
interfere in any way with City performance.  The Contractor further agrees under such circumstances to 
permit the City to use essential Contractor-furnished property.  The City will equitably compensate the 
Contractor for use of such property.  The Contractor will not be entitled to payment for any 
performance period or part thereof during which the City assumes performance pursuant to this 
provision.  This clause does not limit the City's rights under any other provision of this Contract including 
but not limited to "Default," "Termination for the Convenience of the City," and "Inspection of Services."
2.9  PHASE-IN/PHASE-OUT SERVICE - The Contractor recognizes that the services provided by this 
Contract are vital to the City's overall effort; that continuity thereof must be maintained at a 
consistently high level without interruption; that upon expiration of this Contract a successor, either the 
City or another Contractor, may continue these services; that the successor (the City or another 
96 of 351

--- page 97 ---
Contractor) will need phase-in training; and that the Contractor must give his best efforts and 
cooperation in order to effect an orderly and efficient transition to a successor.
In view of the above, the Contractor agrees, upon written notification by the City, to provide 
phase-in/phase-out services for up to 60 days after Contract expiration at the same price as the previous 
period of performance.  After notification, the Contractor agrees to negotiate in good faith with the City 
in determining the nature and extent of the phase-in/phase-out services, including a mutually 
acceptable detailed plan for phase-in/phase-out operations.  The Contractor will be totally responsible 
for providing the services called for by this Contract during any phase-in/phase-out period.
The Contractor agrees to cooperate with the successor, whether it be the City or another Contractor, in 
allowing as many personnel as practical to remain on the job in order to enhance the continuity and 
consistency of the services called for by this Contract.  Toward this end, the Contractor agrees to 
disclose necessary personnel records and to allow its successor to conduct on-site interviews with its 
employees.
2.10  COSTING METHODOLOGY – Contractors are to submit a fixed “BASE” annual target price for 
services based on the proposal. Maintenance, Diagnostic, repair, towing and recovery, body damage, 
per component per vehicle per occurrence up to $1,000.00 will be part of the fixed annual target price.  
Contractor will submit a proposed percentage of “Base” as “Performance Based Compensation” (PBC).  
The successful contractor will be issued a contract for the “Base” amount and the “PBC” amount 
reflected as reserve pending performance review (See 2.13.1.)  If the actual monthly “BASE” costs 
exceed the target price the Contractor will bear the entire difference.  If the actual monthly “BASE” costs 
are less than contracted price the contractor shall only bill for the actual “BASE” costs.  Annual “BASE” 
costs differences will be calculated, and contractor overall cost effectiveness will be considered in the 
“PBC”.  If contractor total “BASE” costs exceed the contract amount by more than 5% the contractor 
may submit in writing prior to annual “PBC” review, the reason(s) for the cost over-run.  Factors that 
may not have been within the Contractor’s ability to control will be considered for total compensation 
review.  
2.11  PAYMENT - The Contractor will submit monthly invoices for services performed during the 
previous month.  After receipt and approval of monthly invoices by the Contracting Officer, payment will 
be due.
2.11.1  Payment is due thirty (30) days after the City has approved the invoice or after the 
Contracting Officer has accepted the services, whichever occurs later.
2.12  COST ADJUSTMENTS - Subject to City approval, cost adjustments for the third and subsequent 
year’s annual fixed amounts will be made using annual indexes of the "Consumer Price Index for All 
Urban Consumers," Bay Area City Average, all items (1967=100) as published in the Monthly Labor 
Review by the U.S. Department of Labor, (CPI). The Contractor will be responsible for calculating CPI 
adjustment factors  based on the most recent February  S.F. Bay Area CPI and submitting a revised 
Exhibit B to the City prior to March 31. Copies of calculations and published indexes of the "Consumer 
Price Index for all Urban Consumers," as identified in this section, will be submitted to the City with each 
adjustment for verification and approval request.

been established by the City relating to downtime, preventive maintenance/statutory inspections and

repair reworks (Section 10).  The Contractor will be expected to meet those standards, minimally, 
without incurring deductions.  If performance falls below these minimum standards the deductions, 
indicated, will be levied against the total monthly “BASE” contract price.  Actual performance will be 
tracked on the Computerized Fleet Management System.  The Contractor shall explain in writing the 
reason that service category(s) did not meet the minimum performance standard and how performance 
will be returned to acceptable levels.  The Contracting Officer will evaluate the Contractor's explanation 
and determine if full payment, partial payment, or the contract termination process is applicable.  If the 
contractor’s actual “BASE” costs for services
2.13.1  PERFORMANCE BASED COMPENSATION (PBC).  The PBC is intended to be a portion of the 
contractor’s acceptable profit margin and therefore an incentive to both meet and exceed 
performance standards.  The criteria for evaluating the PBC will overall Contractor performance 
and a set of Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) established by the City.  The KPIs shall be specific, 
defined, reasonable, measurable and as objective as possible.  Examples of KPI types are:  
Performance Standards, Contractor Cost Savings/Control, Innovation, Customer Focus. PBC will 
be reviewed quarterly and up to 25% of annual PBC may be awarded upon quarterly review.  
Quarterly, the Contractor and the City will examine the Performance Standards and the Key 
Performance Indicators to determine and evaluate the service levels, in the event of subpar 
performance, guidance will be provided to assist the Contract toward improvement upon 
identified areas. 
2.14  ACCEPTANCE OF REPERFORMANCE OR LATE PERFORMANCE.  Re-performance or late performance 
rights should be an exception rather than the rule in a performance work statement.  The Contractor is 
expected to ensure performance to standard through the quality control system.
2.15  Except as otherwise provided by this section, the services required by this contract are of such 
nature that defective or incomplete performance disclosed by City inspection is not subject to correction 
by re-performance or late performance, and the Contractor shall not be required or entitled to re-
perform, perform late, or otherwise correct defective services for the purpose of improving an existing 
inspection rating or avoiding a reduction in the full contract price.
2.16  At the sole election of the City and upon notification to the Contractor, the Contractor may be 
required to re-perform or perform late any or all defective work disclosed by City inspection including 
defective and incomplete performance.  Where the City so elects, the Contractor shall be notified 
promptly after inspection that specified defective services will be re-performed or performed late, and 
completed within a reasonable time specified by the City.  In such cases, the City shall re-inspect work 
designated for re-performance or late performance, and the Contractor will pay any damages sustained 
by the City including, for example, the costs associated with re-inspection.
2.17  METHOD OF PAYMENT - The Contract Charges accruing during a given calendar month will be 
tendered to the Contractor at the Contractor's then-current address for notices.  If all of the data 
necessary to compute any Contract Charges (and any credits or offsets) are not available in time to 
make such payment when due, the City may make a good faith estimate of such data and compute the 
payment accordingly.
2.17.1  Adjustments to such payment will be made on the succeeding monthly payment after the 
necessary data are available.  The City will not operate on the basis of estimates beyond thirty 
(30) calendar days.
2.17.2  Contractor will submit invoices on a monthly basis in arrears for services provided in 
accordance with contract requirements.  (Annual Contract Price/12 months less (-) any

2.17.4  City shall pay invoice within thirty (30) days of submission after the City has approved the

2.18  OUT-OF-CONTRACT WORK – Out of Contract work will be the balance of any single component 
repair or a single body work event greater than $1,000. Out of Contract work must be approved by the 
City upon diagnosis and an estimate documenting all costs must be provided. 
Out of Contract work may include pass through invoices which will be invoiced by the Contractor to the 
City at Contractor’s actual cost. All repairs, diagnostics, maintenance, inspections, required testing and 
body damage or negligence  up to $1,000.00 shall be part of the Fixed Annual Target Price and identified 
in the “BASE” cost proposal form. Contractor shall provide a written estimate for all directed work (i.e. 
adding lights, accessories, fabrication, etc.) and requires prior approval from an authorized manager in 
either writing or email acknowledgement prior to commencing work. No payment shall be made for 
unauthorized Out-of-Contract work. All Out-of-Contract work shall be at time and materials, at the 
hourly rate listed in Contractor’s cost proposal.
2.18.1 REPAIRS. All repairs, diagnostics, maintenance, inspections, required testing, keys, key 
fobs, body damage or negligence up to $1,000.00 per component or body work occurrence shall 
be part of the Fixed Annual Target Price and identified in the “BASE” cost proposal form. 
Repair costs exceeding $1,000 per repair component, or body work occurrence shall constitute an 
“OUT OF CONTRACT” repair as in 2.18 above. Costs in excess of $1,000 will be the responsibility 
of the City and must be approved by the City at time of diagnosis, post repair approval will not be 
granted, and it will be the Contractor’s responsibility to cover those costs. * Repair component 
examples- alternator, starter, cylinder head.   Repair component shall include the associated labor 
(Mitchell / ALLDATA labor guide) for replacement of the component – exclusive of diagnostic or 
other collateral components or services.
2.18.2 At any time during the contract term, the Contracting Officer, by written notice, may 
increase the Scope of Work, make changes in operating and maintenance requirements, add 
additional vehicles and equipment to the fleet, or request repairs and services not covered by the 
basic contract, as he may find necessary to accomplish the general purpose of the work and 
service contracted for.  Any and all work or service performed by written notice by the Contractor 
will be performed in accordance with all requirements of the General Conditions and 
Specifications of this RFP, plus any special provisions, and any specifications or special 
instructions issued to execute the extra or changed work.
2.18.3 Whenever the Contractor receives a written notice, the Contractor will furnish (any or all, 
as requested in the written notice) the necessary manpower, service, parts, material, equipment, 
99 of 351

--- page 100 ---
components or appurtenances required to accomplish the repair, work or service described in the 
Add Notice.  Such repair, work or service will be completed within the applicable time when 
prescribed, but if no applicable completion time is prescribed, the work will be completed within

2.18.4 Any item provided pursuant to a written notice must comply with the Contract and will be 
subject to the same reports, and inspections as well as acceptance or rejection in the same 
manner as any specific task herein described.
It is understood that the costs associated with Out-Of-Contract Work will be invoiced separately

City will pay the pass-through expense of Contractor’s lease of the new site. If no site is available within 
the City of San Mateo for a reasonable cost, City and Contractor will negotiate the terms of Contractor’s 
relocation. If City and Contractor are not able to reach agreement regarding the terms of Contractor’s 
relocation, City may terminate this agreement with six (6) months notice to contractor.

contract start date.

3.0 to 3.2 RESERVED 
3.3  SURVIVAL - Notwithstanding the City's acceptance of services and payment of any charges or 
purchase price therefore, and notwithstanding the expiration of the Service Term, the Contractor will 
remain obligated to the City under all clauses of this Contract which expressly or by their nature extend 
beyond and survive such acceptance and payment.
3.4  FORCE MAJEURE - Timely performance by both parties is essential to this contract.  However, 
neither the Contractor nor the City will be liable for delays in performing its obligations to the extent the 
delay is caused by Force Majeure, provided that no time extension because of Force Majeure will ever 
be allowed unless:  (a) promptly upon the occurrence of a Force Majeure, the party whose performance 
is delayed thereby will provide the other party with written notice of the cause and extent thereof as 
well as request for a time extension equal to the estimated duration thereof; and (b) within seven (7) 
calendar days of the cessation of the Force Majeure, the party whose performance was delayed will 
provide the other party with written notice of the actual delay incurred, upon receipt of which the time 
of the delayed performance will be extended for the time actually lost by reason of the Force Majeure.

3.5  NON-WAIVER - Failure of the City to insist upon strict performance of any of the terms and 
conditions hereof, or failure or delay to exercise any rights or remedies provided herein or by law, or 
failure of the City to notify the  Contractor properly in the event of default, or review of or approval of 
any plans or specifications will not release the Contractor from any of the obligations of this contract, 
and will not be deemed a waiver of any right of the City to insist upon strict performance hereof or any

3.7  RESERVED
3.8  DEFAULT BY THE CITY – Default by the City will occur if the City fails to perform or observe any  
material, rather than minor,  terms and conditions of this contract required to be performed or 
observed by the City.  Should such a  material default occur, the Contractor will have the right to 
terminate all or part of its duties under this contract as of the 30th day following the receipt by the City 
of a notice from the Contractor describing such material default and intended termination, provided: (1) 
such termination will be ineffective if within said 30-day period the City cures said material default and 
(2) such termination may be stayed, at the sole option of the Contractor, pending cure of said material 
default.
3.9  DEFAULT BY THE CONTRACTOR - Default by the Contractor will occur if:  (1) the Contractor fails to 
perform or observe any of the terms or conditions of this Contract required to be performed or 
observed by it; or (2) the Contractor is dissolved or liquidated; the Contractor files a petition in 
bankruptcy; the Contractor is adjudicated as a bankrupt; the Contractor makes an assignment for the 
benefit of creditors; a court of competent jurisdiction assignment for the benefit of creditors; a court of 
competent jurisdiction approves any petition or other pleading in any action seeking reorganization, 
arrangement, adjustment or composition of or in respect of the Contractor under the federal 
bankruptcy laws or any similar federal or state laws; or a receiver, trustee or similar official for the 
Contractor, or the Contractor's property, is appointed, and such appointment remains in effect for sixty 
(60) days or more.
Should such a material default occur, the Contracting Officer will have the right to terminate all or part 
of the City's duties under this Contract as of the 30th day following the receipt by the Contractor of a 
notice from the Contracting Officer describing such material default and intended termination, 
provided:  (1) such termination will be ineffective if within said 30-day period the Contractor cures said 
default, and (2) such termination may be stayed, at the sole option of the Contracting Officer, pending 
cure of said material default.
3.10  RESERVED

but will be cumulative of all rights and remedies now or hereafter existing whether by statute, at law, or 
in equity; provided, however, neither party may terminate its duties under this contract except in 
accordance with the provisions hereof.

Availability Performance Exhibit.

accordance with approved plans of abatement subject to city-wide priorities.  Prior to any modification

case of alterations necessary for OSHA compliance, such permission shall not be reasonably withheld.  
The Contractor shall return the facilities to the City in the same condition as received, normal use and

5.1.2  Equipment.  The City shall provide the Contractor with equipment listed in Technical Attachment 
C.  The Contractor is responsible for maintaining all City furnished equipment.  Maintenance will be 
performed throughout the performance period in accordance with approved commercial practices.  
Contingent with funding, the City will replace equipment only when it is no longer usable for its 
intended purpose due to fair wear and tear.  
5.1.2.1  Equipment Inventory.  Not later than five (5) days prior to start of the basic contract period, the 
Contractor and a City representative shall conduct a joint inventory of all City furnished equipment. The 
Contractor shall receipt for all equipment provided by the City.  The Contractor and a City representative 
shall jointly determine the working order and condition of all equipment.  Items of equipment missing or 
not in working order shall be recorded.  The City will replace missing items and repair all items not in 
working order or the Contracting Officer will direct the Contractor to replace the missing item(s) or 
accomplish the repair and the Contractor will be reimbursed as preagreed costs.
The City Representative will give disposition instructions for items beyond repair.  The Contractor and 
the City Representative shall certify their agreement as to the working order of the equipment.  If the 
Contractor does not participate in the inventory, the Contractor must accept as accurate the listing(s) 
and stated condition of equipment provided by the City.  If the Contractor participates in the inventory, 
but does not agree with the City Representative's determination as to the working order of the 
equipment, this failure of the Contractor to agree on working order and defects shall be treated as a 
dispute pursuant to the clause of this contract entitled, "Disputes".
5.1.2.2  Equipment Accounting.  The Contractor shall designate custodians and alternates to receipt and 
account for City furnished equipment.  This equipment is designated in Technical Attachment C.
5.1.2.3  Obtaining Additional or Replacement Equipment.  The Contractor shall submit requests for 
additional or replacement City furnished equipment required in the performance of the contract.  The 
Contractor shall submit such requests through to the Contracting Officer for approval and any 
appropriate contract modification.  Upon approval, the Contractor shall obtain the equipment by placing 
orders for such items through the Contracting Officer.  Equipment purchased by the Contractor without 
Contracting Officer’s authorization shall be paid for by the Contractor.
5.1.2.4  Equipment Accountability.  Thirty days prior to completion of the contract, a joint inventory of 
equipment shall be conducted by the Contractor and a City representative.  The Contractor shall be 
liable for loss or damage to City furnished property beyond fair wear and tear.  Compensation shall be 
effected either by reduced amounts owed to the Contractor or by direct payment from the Contractor, 
the method to be determined by the Contracting Officer.  All equipment in need of repairs/maintenance 
shall be repaired/maintained by the Contractor within 30 days of discovery, but before the joint 
inventory is made.  All repairs/maintenance not performed by the Contractor shall be made at the City's 
option and at the Contractor's expense.  In the case of damaged property, the amount of compensation 
due the City by the Contractor shall be actual cost of repair, provided such amount does not exceed the

economical value.  In the case of loss or damage beyond economical repair to equipment, the amount of

dispute pursuant to the clause of this contract entitled "Disputes".
5.1.2.5  Disposition of Equipment.  When equipment is determined to be beyond economical repair, the

CONTRACTOR-FURNISHED ITEMS AND SERVICES
6.1  GENERAL.  The Contractor shall furnish everything required to perform all services required by this 
performance work statement.  Except for those items or services specifically stated to be City furnished.
6.2  CONTRACTOR-FURNISHED ITEMS AND SERVICES.
6.2.1  Parts and Supplies.  The Contractor will furnish at his own expense all parts required to perform 
the maintenance and repair work described in this Contract The Contractor will be responsible to ensure 
that parts are available to meet the operations essential requirements of this Contract, and to maintain 
the performance of the work described in this Contract to acceptable quality levels.  The Contractor shall 
provide his own vehicle for parts pickup.
6.2.2 Batteries.  The Contractor shall provide all batteries.  Batteries shall have adequate CCA and 
reserve capacity to meet the load requirements of the vehicles, including all accessories.  The 
group size should correspond to the application.  CCA, reserve capacity, and group size of 
106 of 351

--- page 107 ---
replacement batteries shall be no less than that of the original equipment battery. Batteries deemed 
dead 12.4 volts or less must be recharged or replaced. Vehicles failing a minimum battery voltage are to 
be considered Out of Service until battery is fully charged or replaced. 
6.2.3  Oil Lubrication Products.  The Contractor shall provide all oil and lubrication products, including 
addon oil, required in the performance of the work described in this Contract.  Contractor shall 
provide recycled oil that has been certified as re-refined oil which meets or exceeds these 
specifications by the American Petroleum Institute (API). Contractor furnished products shall 
meet the requirements established by the vehicle manufacturers.
6.2.4  Tires.  Contractor shall provide all tires and be responsible for their proper disposal.  Tires shall 
meet the requirements established by the vehicle or equipment manufacturers.  Tires will be replaced 
when the tread reaches 4/32”, Except police patrol vehicles which shall be replaced when the tread 
depth reaches 5/32”. Or when a tire has aged beyond 84 Months of manufacture date. 
6.2.5  Hazardous Waste.  The Contractor shall control, provide for and dispose of all hazardous waste 
materials generated from the performance of this contract including: oil, fuel, coolant, brake fluid, 
hydraulic fluid, power steering fluid, solvents, batteries, asbestos, oil filters, fuel filters, transmission 
filter, hydraulic filters, tires, brake pads / Brake materials, contaminated grease sweep, etc., according to 
all applicable laws and regulations.  
6.2.6  Hand Tools.  The Contractor shall ensure that each Technician has adequate tools to perform the 
required repairs and services as set forth in this contract. Contractor to provide insurance for each 
technician’s tools & toolbox(es) against theft, damage, and loss to include fire, flood and earthquake.
6.2.7  Computer and Software.  The Contractor shall provide a Computerized Fleet Maintenance 
Information system capable of providing computerized records and scheduling of preventive 
maintenance on the vehicles and equipment detailed in this Contract, and other computerized records 
pursuant to this Contract as required.  Computerized Records and Schedules will include as a minimum 
those listed in Technical Attachment C.  Upon termination of this contract, the Contractor shall provide 
the City or successor with current and historical cost/productivity data and software as may be required 
for phasein/phaseout.
The Contract is to provide real time functionality for Heads Up Display such as internet connected TV to 
display vehicles under the shop control – Vehicle detail  to include unit number, department, Service 
Request,  date & time in, current status (e.g. Diag, pending tech waiting on parts, etc.), notes, and 
estimated time & date of completion. This system must be accessible to remote end users and offer 
department filter capability.
All records/data maintained during the term of the contract shall remain the property of the City.
6.2.8  Custodial Service.  In all facilities furnished by the City, the Contractor shall maintain the facilities 
in such a condition that would not jeopardize safety, be conducive to fire hazards or cause deterioration 
of the facilities.  Wash and rest areas will be kept clean and litter will be removed.
6.2.8  Physical Security.  The Contractor shall be responsible for safeguarding all City property in its work 
area.  At the close of each work period, facilities and equipment shall be secured.
6.3  TELEPHONE SERVICE.  The Contractor shall use existing telephone lines and will bear the cost of 
usage.
107 of 351

--- page 108 ---
6.4.  REMOVAL OF CONTRACTOR PROPERTY.  Upon completion of the contract, a City representative will 
observe the removal of incumbent Contractor's equipment from installation premises:  all Contractor 
equipment, supplies, and materials will be removed.  The facilities being vacated by the outgoing 
Contractor shall be cleaned to the satisfaction of the City.
6.5  GROUNDS MAINTENANCE.  The Contractor shall be responsible for policing his assigned grounds, 
sidewalks, storage and parking areas.  This includes at least 50 feet from outside wall of furnished 
facilities.
6.6  REPAIR AND REPLACEMENT PARTS.
6.6.1  The Contractor shall provide motor vehicle and equipment repair parts equal in quality to 
replacement parts supplied by the original equipment manufacturer.
6.6.2  Commercially purchased or Contractor rebuilt parts may be used if they equal or exceed the 
quality of the original parts.
6.6.3  Used parts may be used only on an exception basis when other sources have been exhausted and 
with written approval of the Contract Officer.  Used parts include cannibalized parts from City furnished 
vehicles.
6.6.4  The Contractor will be responsible to assure that parts are available to meet the requirements of 
the Contract.    
6.6.5  Replacement Parts.  The Contractor shall furnish all replacement parts.  Quality of parts shall be 
equal to or better than the parts in the equipment when the equipment was turned over by the City.
SECTION 7
SPECIFIC TASKS
7.1  VEHICLE MAINTENANCE.
7.1.1  General.  The Contractor shall maintain vehicles and equipment listed in Technical Attachment B 
to meet standards established by the original equipment manufacturer and as further amended by 
directives stated in this Contract.  The Contractor shall perform maintenance, diagnostic, and repair 
service on all units covered by this contract in the facilities provided for this service, or in the field as 
required. Third party vendors may be utilized on a case by case basis and as approved by the City 
Contracting Officer.
 
7.1.1.1  The Contractor shall maintain vehicle and equipment listed in Technical Attachment B to meet 
standards; including scheduled and unscheduled maintenance.
7.1.1.1.1  Repair of vehicles damaged by accident, abuse and incident are the responsibility of the 
Contractor up to $1,000.00 per occurrence. All repair costs beyond this limit are to be approved by the 
City Contracting Officer. Contracting Officer is to be advised in advance of the commencement of any 
vehicle body repairs.
7.1.1.3  If a vehicle repair estimate exceeds the component repair limit, the Contractor shall submit the 
requirement to the Contracting Officer.  The portion of the costs that exceeds the component repair 
108 of 351

--- page 109 ---
limit shall be worked and paid in accordance with the over and above procedures outlined in this 
Contract.  The repair cost will be authorized by the Contracting Officer and the Contractor prior to 
performing the work.  VOC calculations stop when the City Representative receives the repair estimate 
and starts again when the Contracting Officer gives approval for the repair.  If it is determined that the 
repair limit will not be exceeded, the VOC is calculated from the time the vehicle enters the shop.
7.1.1.4
Repair Parts.
7.1.1.4.1  The Contractor shall provide motor vehicle and equipment repair parts equal in quality to 
replacement parts supplied by the original equipment manufacturer.
7.1.1.4.2  Commercially purchased or Contractor rebuilt parts may be approved by the Contracting 
Officer on a case by case basis. Such parts must be of equal or superior quality of the original parts.
7.1.1.4.3  Used parts may be used only on an exception basis with Contracting Officer approval when 
other sources have been exhausted or when it is economically or chronologically advantageous to the 
City. Used parts include cannibalization of parts from City furnished vehicles.
7.1.1.4.4  Invoices for all parts purchased by the Contractor from any source shall be maintained for the 
duration of contract and options.  The invoice and sales slip files shall be made available to the City upon 
request.  Parts charged to individual vehicles shall be priced at Contractor's acquisition cost and sales 
slips will be attached to and filed with the work order.
7.1.1.5  Vehicle warranty work will be the responsibility of the Contractor.  All warranty work that is out 
of commission and is not the fault of the Contractor will not be counted in VOC calculations.  
Documentation of follow up actions shall be maintained and provided to the City every 10 days.
Scheduling, Vehicle Conveyance to and from warranty work is the responsibility of the Contractor.
7.1.1.6
Radio Installation, Maintenance and Repair.
7.1.1.6.1  The Contractor shall be responsible for coordinating the maintenance and repair of radio 
equipment with an approved vendor. These costs will be covered by the Contactor up to $1,000.00 per 
vehicle per occurrence.
7.1.1.6.2  The Contractor shall submit requests for the repair of radio equipment through the 
Contracting Officer.  
7.1.1.6.3  The Contractor shall be responsible for repair and associated costs of Contractor caused 
damage to radio equipment.
7.1.1.7  Vehicle Accessory and Special Equipment.  An item added to a vehicle to meet an operational 
requirement will be purchased by the vehicle using activity (requestor) and will be installed and 
maintained by the vehicle maintenance Contractor.  The item will be transferred from one vehicle and 
installed on another vehicle upon receipt of an approved authorization.  Examples of accessory and 
special equipment are spotlights, spare tire racks, mirrors, horns, lights, campers, cargo shells, hydraulic 
tail gates, towing hitches, winches, etc.
7.2  MINOR REPAIR.  The Contractor shall:
109 of 351

--- page 110 ---
7.2.1  Provide a quick turnaround repair service for repairs estimated to take one half hour or less.  
Repairs shall begin not later than 5 minutes after arrival of vehicle.
7.2.2  Operate a tire facility to provide repair, replacement and balancing of vehicle tires.  Remove and 
reinstall mounted tires (includes unscheduled roadside service).  Repair of flat tires will be by patching 
or patch/ plugging.  Tire sealant is not to be utilized unless specifically authorized by the City on a case 
by case basis.  Provide in contract dismount and disposal of orphan or cast off tire and rim assemblies. 
7.3  ROAD CALLS.  The Contractor shall provide onsite scheduled and unscheduled maintenance, 
diagnostics and repair for vehicles which because of design or immobility cannot be economically 
delivered to the vehicle maintenance facility.
7.3.1  Service calls to start, repair, or unlock vehicles that are disabled away from the shop area are the 
responsibility of the Contractor.  Service calls shall be responded to immediately. Once Contractor is 
notified of a disabled vehicle, Contractor shall provide City staff with an estimated time for tow/repair 
service. Contractor shall provide this update  within  thirty (30) minutes of  the original call for service. 
Contractor shall make necessary arrangements for tow service or repair within one (1) hour from 
original time of service call. All service calls will be recorded.  A service call control register using a 
consecutive numbering system will be maintained and these will be retained for the duration of the 
contract period.
7.3.2 AFTER HOURS/EMERGENCY SERVICE.  Contractor shall provide an emergency contact telephone 
number for after hours and/or emergency service.
7.4  MAJOR REPAIR.  Contractor is responsible for:
7.4.1  Repair or replacement of parts, assemblies, sub-assemblies, and components.
7.4.2  Fabrication or parts when required (weld, lathe work, etc.)
7.4.3  Glass replacement. The Contractor shall provide glass & mirror services, or have an approved third 
party vendor available as an on call basis. Glass shall be of an OEM approved type and tint. Where 
plastic film tint is utilized, the vendor will provide these services or an approved third party. Where units 
are fitted with Advanced Driver Safety Devices – those items shall be calibrated by an authorized vendor 
or the OEM dealer upon windshield replacement.
7.4.4  Body and Frame Repair (Major).  Major or extensive body work shall be performed by a qualified 
body shop.  The Contractor shall be responsible for arranging and managing the repairs of wrecked 
vehicles through an outside body shop.  Before releasing a damaged or wrecked vehicle for repairs, the 
Contractor shall obtain three proposals on the repairs.  Proposals shall include labor rates, and itemized 
cost for parts and labor.  The Contractor shall submit the proposals to the Contracting Officer for 
approval to proceed.  If the cost of repairing the unit exceeds its service value to the City, the 
Contracting Officer will review with the Contractor the cost-effectiveness of repairs versus replacement.  
Invoices for major body work performed by an outside body shop will be accepted solely by the 
Contractor, who will be reimbursed by the City at cost.
7.4.5  Body Repair (Minor).  Minor repair (under $1,000.00) on vehicle bodies, trim, decals, logos, glass 
replacement, mirror, Camera systems, painting, corrosion control and upholstery repair shall be 
accomplished as necessary to preserve safe operation and maintain the City image. Paint shall meet or 
exceed original equipment manufacturer's specifications.
110 of 351

--- page 111 ---
7.4.6  Painting and Marking.  The Contractor is responsible to maintain the overall image of the City 
fleet. Decals, logos and wraps will be maintained and replaced as needed by the Contractor. A qualified 
body and paint shop will perform all painting of vehicles and corrosion control; however, complete 
vehicle/equipment painting to maintain cosmetic appearance shall be accomplished only when required 
and approved by the Contracting Officer.  Paint shall meet or exceed original equipment manufacturers 
specifications. City logos, decals and wraps will be of premium quality and of design, color and size as 
approved by the City.
7.4.7  Upholstery Repair.  Contractor is responsible for the repair and replacement of damaged, worn or 
threadbare upholstery, seating hardware and door panels.  Material used in upholstery repair will meet 
or exceed original manufacturer's specifications and be of matching color. City Approved Seat Covers 
may be substituted upon special request.
7.4.8  Recalls, Technical Order modifications, service bulletins, and approved local modifications will, 
where applicable, be accomplished by the manufacturer (or designee).  If not applicable, Contractor will 
perform same and will be reimbursed for parts and labor on an "over and above" basis. Vehicle 
Conveyance to and from manufacturer for the purposes of such items as described will be the 
responsibility of the Contractor. 
7.4.9  Seasonal Equipment Repair.  The Contractor shall establish a program to ensure seasonal 
equipment is fully serviceable at the start of the season.  At the conclusion of the season, equipment to 
be stored shall be properly protected to include fuel stabilization and fogging along with any other 
storage preparations.
7.4.10  Corrosion Control.  Corrosion control shall be accomplished by the Contractor. Early stages of 
corrosion are to be treated with a rust inhibitor or converter and paint sealed (e.g. SEM “rust mort”, CRC 
rust converter, etc.)
7.4.11  Delayed Maintenance Program.  Contractor shall complete all delayed maintenance at the 
earliest possible date.  As a minimum, it shall be completed on the next scheduled/unscheduled work 
order, not to exceed 180 calendar days from the last date the vehicle was seen for 
scheduled/unscheduled maintenance.  If work consists of deferred parts and said parts are backordered 
for over 30 days, follow-up on parts will immediately be accomplished and documented.  Follow-up shall 
be done every 5 working days thereafter and documentation provided to the City.
7.4.12  Provide Scheduled Maintenance and Service.  The Contractor shall be responsible for the 
following: 
a. Providing a comprehensive Preventive Maintenance Program. 
b. Adherence to the vehicle / equipment manufacturer’s scheduled maintenance guidelines
c. CNG Annual inspection 
d. Smog inspections will be performed in accordance with California State Regulations (biannual 
program). 
e. HD/IM- Diesel powered vehicles requiring mandated HD/IM testing shall be performed by the 
Contractor. 
f. BIT - Contractor will comply with the state's "Biennial Inspection of Terminals" (BIT) Program by 
performing the appropriate inspections and keeping proper maintenance and driver's records. 
g. Aerial Devices - Contractor shall perform or provide through a certified third party provider 
annual inspections and dielectric testing for aerial type equipment.  The Contractor shall assure 
the safety inspection and preventive maintenance programs are accomplished during the month 
it is scheduled. 
h. Other Regulatory Compliance 
111 of 351

--- page 112 ---
7.4.13  Shipment and Storage of Vehicles.  The Contractor shall process vehicles as directed by the City. 
Contractor employees shall only park in the city’s employee lot or on street. Employees are not 
permitted to operate their vehicles within the Corporation Yard without City approval.
7.4.14  Receiving New Vehicles and Equipment.  The Contracting Officer shall coordinate receipt and 
delivery of all new fleet vehicles and equipment through the Contractor and the City.  The Contractor 
shall prepare and maintain files for all new vehicles added to the fleet.
7.4.15  Salvage Vehicles and Equipment.  Units scheduled for salvage will be removed from the 
Contractor's active files.  The Contractor shall assist the City in determining when fleet vehicles and 
equipment have reached their optimum period of retention.  Contractor is responsible for 
decommissioning of Salvage units.
7.4.16 Decommissioning Vehicles and Equipment. The Contractor is responsible and shall include in the 
Fixed Annual Target Price for the decommissioning of City owned vehicles in preparation for auction sale 
or disposal. This includes removing all decals, license plates and, City owned equipment such as two-way 
radios, specialty safety lighting and equipment not originally equipped when vehicle was placed into 
service.  Vehicles are to be cleaned and washed prior to dispatch to auction. The City may, at their 
discretion, send some specialty vehicles to a third party vendor for specialty equipment 
decommissioning.  A typical example may include patrol car decommissioning. Decommissioning  shall 
be performed in a timely manner and items to be redeployed are to be stored  onsite until they can be 
reinstalled.
7.5  ADMINISTRATION.
7.5.1  The Contractor shall provide information concerning the maintenance status (for example, 
awaiting parts, estimated time in commission, etc.) of vehicles in the vehicle maintenance facility upon 
request. Contractor will provide functionality for a continuously updated, remotely viewable heads-up 
display type system to report to each end user department the current vehicle status. 
7.5.2  The Contractor shall maintain a log to reflect the current status of manufacturer recalls, technical 
service bulletins and local modifications.  Contractor is responsible for scheduling, conveyance and 
completion of recalls, technical service bulletins and local modifications.
7.5.3  The Contractor shall maintain a work order control register for the duration of the contract and 
shall issue all work order numbers.  A consecutive numbering system shall be used. Work order system 
must reflect the City vehicle numbering system, vehicle year, make, model, assigned department along 
with date stamps for vehicle time in and completion along with a technician work hours log. This system 
is to be accessible to the City and shall be delivered to the city in digital form upon conclusion of the 
contract.
7.5.4  The Contractor shall maintain historical information of repair actions on each vehicle utilizing a 
City approved Fleet Maintenance Software System. The City is to have access to the Fleet Management 
Software and this historical data is to be supplied to the city in digital form upon the conclusion of the 
contract.
7.5.5  The Contractor shall comply with documentation requirements for vehicle accident/abuse in 
accordance with City requirements.
