--- page 113 ---
7.5.6  The Contractor shall attend local meetings pertaining to vehicle maintenance, and safety as 
required by the Contracting Officer or City Representative.
7.5.7  The Contractor shall provide records, reports, and analysis as specified in the reports section.  
Analysis will consist of a written in-depth assessment of all collected data to verbally explain what, 
when, why, and how actions occurred and recommendations to resolve any deficient area.
7.5.8  When requested, the Contractor shall prepare and submit budget estimates for City provided 
supplies (fuel, parts, supplies etc.) to the Contracting Officer.
7.5.9  Maintenance Manuals and Shop Manuals.  The City has many of the maintenance manuals which 
will be turned over to the Contractor at the start of the contract period; however, it shall remain the 
Contractor's responsibility to obtain missing manuals and documents, and to update 
maintenance/repair manuals regularly.  All Maintenance manuals shall become property of the City 
upon completion of the contract.
7.5.10  Technical Advisor.  The Contractor shall act in the capacity of technical advisor to the City 
regarding the acquisition of new vehicles and equipment and shall provide historical maintenance data 
on proposed equipment as may be useful in determining selection of vehicles.
7.5.11  Correspondence.  The Contractor shall prepare Vehicle Maintenance and Analysis related 
correspondence.  Correspondence shall consist of replies, requests for assistance, suggestions (including 
evaluations), and other routine correspondence.  Correspondence shall be answered in a timely manner.
7.6  POLICING THE GROUNDS.  The Contractor shall be responsible for keeping the grounds around the 
facilities and interior shop areas, which the Contractor occupies, free of debris and litter. Vehicles under 
the Contractor’s control shall be safely parked, secured, locked and keys secured in a lock box inside the 
Fleet Garage.
7.7  VEHICLE ABUSE.  The Contractor shall document areas of vehicle abuse, and furnish evidence of 
breakdown or failure due to suspected abuse to the Contracting Officer.  The Contracting Officer will 
assess the evidence and may rule not to penalize the Contractor and to address the repair through 
Vehicle Rehabilitation.
7.8  ACCIDENTS.  The Contractor shall record and report promptly to the Contracting Officer all available 
facts related to each instance of damage to City vehicles while being operated by Contractor personnel, 
and each instance of injury to either Contractor or City personnel.  All accidents involving City of San 
Mateo vehicles must be reported and documented in accordance with the City's Accidents Involving City 
Vehicles policy.
7.9  EQUIPMENT MAINTENANCE.  The Contractor is responsible for maintenance and repair of the City 
furnished equipment listed in Technical Attachment C.
7.9.1  Minor Maintenance.  Shall include cleaning, adjusting, ordinary lubrications, tightening of nuts and 
bolts, and preventive maintenance actions recommended by the equipment manufacturer and the City.
7.9.2  Major Maintenance.  Shall include repair of inoperable equipment, replacing components, parts, 
filters, hinges, gaskets, compressors, etc.
7.9.3  Repair Limits.  The Contractor is responsible for individual unit repair costs up to $1,000 per 
113 of 351

--- page 114 ---
component, per occurrence to include parts, consumables, and associated labor (industry standard labor 
guide – i.e. Mitchell, ALLDATA.) At Contract agreed labor rate - If no labor guide is available for the 
repair, Contractor will consult City Fleet manager. Repair costs to include Diagnostics, Preventive 
Maintenance, repairs, glass, keys, key FOBS, breakdowns / towing, body damage, or abuse.  Body 
damage repaired in a single event will be considered a single occurrence in which the $1,000 will 
function as a deductible. Rework required due to faulty diagnostics, repair or parts shall be the sole 
responsibility of the contractor.  
7.9.4  Repairs on Rolling Stock.  The Contractor shall perform all maintenance, diagnostics and repairs on 
rolling stock as required.  Routine repairs include, but are not limited to hitches, wheels, bearings, seals, 
safety lights and electrical wiring harnesses.
7.9.5  Repairs to Stationary Equipment.  The Contractor shall perform all maintenance, diagnostics, and 
repairs on stationary equipment (i.e., standby generators).
7.9.6 Vehicle Master Key Library. The Contractor shall maintain spare Keys & Key FOBS for all City 
vehicles. The City has an existing inventory and provides duplicates upon new vehicle acquisition.  The 
Contractor will provide replacement keys and FOBs in the event of end user or Contractor loss. The 
Contractor shall provide secure locking key storage and regularly complete an inventory of Keys & FOBs 
ensuring every unit has a spare set in the master Key Library.  Costs of maintaining the Keys and FOBs 
shall be covered under BASE contract.
7.9.7 Vehicle On-Site Charging. On occasion it may be necessary for EV units to be charged, or vehicles 
repositioned within the Corp Yard charging infrastructure. The Contractor is uniquely positioned to 
access such units and may be called upon to act as a liaison for these needs as they arise. Contractor 
agrees to provide those services at no charge to the City.
7.9.8 Interim Maintenance Items.   The Contractor shall provide support for interim maintenance items. 
Interim maintenance items are periodic tasks that occur outside of a typical PM cycle. These items often 
include services such as- tire inflation, wiper blade replacement, grease points, sweeper broom 
replacement, lawn mower blade sharpening or other services. The Contractor will provide a convenient 
means to coordinate these “on-demand” services and prioritize technician support to ensure these tasks 
are completed in a timely manner. 
7.9.9 BATTERY SHOP.  Operate a battery shop to provide replacement batteries and battery services for 
all equipment. Establish a baseline battery inventory and ensure batteries are charged and ready for 
installation.
7.9.10 TOWING, RECOVERY AND ROADSIDE ASSISTANCE   The Contractor will be responsible for 
providing towing/recovery of disabled vehicles/equipment. Towing to also include conveyance of a 
vehicle to and from a third-party vendor as needed. Roadside assistance to include: flat tires 
replacement, lock out / lost keys, “dead” battery replacement or other roadside mechanical repair. 
7.10
MOBILITY DEPLOYMENT, DISASTER PREPAREDNESS AND OTHER CONTINGENCY/
EXERCISES.
7.10.1  Upon notification, the Contractor shall provide vehicle maintenance to support activation or 
exercise of contingency operations or plans.
7.10.2  The Contractor shall appoint a manager/supervisor to represent Fleet Services at the Emergency 
Operations Center (Logistics Section) during emergency drills/activation.
114 of 351

--- page 115 ---
7.10.3  The Contractor shall provide vehicle maintenance 24 hours a day, seven days a week, if required, 
for the duration of the contingency.
7.10.4  The Contractor shall use the priorities established by the City if the activation or exercise of 
multiple contingency plans generates conflicting support requirements.  If the Contractor cannot 
accomplish a routine workload due to activation or exercise or any contingency plan, reductions in 
payment, based upon the performance requirements, summary shall not be made for non-support of 
the lower priorities.
7.10.5  The Contractor shall submit, on contract start date, a plan for providing the maximum required 
support.  The plan must be approved by the Contracting Officer.
7.11
EMERGENCY OPERATIONS.
7.11.1 Upon notification by the Contracting Officer, the Contractor shall provide vehicle maintenance 
diagnostic, and repair  to support national commitments, up to and including a declared war.
7.11.2  The Contractor shall appoint a manager/supervisor to represent Fleet Services at the Emergency 
Operations Center (Logistics Section) during emergency drills/activation.
7.11.3  The Contractor shall provide vehicle maintenance 24 hours a day, seven days a week, as 
required, for the duration of the emergency.  The Contracting Officer shall advise the Contractor verbally 
of the required level of effort and follow up with a written change to the contract.  A supplemental 
agreement shall be negotiated to compensate for services over and above the normal workload, 
pursuant to the "changes" clause of this contract.
SECTION 8
INDUSTRIAL SAFETY REQUIREMENTS
8.1
GENERAL REQUIREMENTS.
8.1.1  Mishap Reporting and Investigation:
8.1.1.1  The Contractor shall report within one hour to the Contracting Officer all pertinent facts 
relating to each case of damage to City property or lost time injury.
8.1.1.2  If the City decides to investigate the mishap, the Contractor shall cooperate fully and 
assist the City personnel until the investigation is completed.
8.1.2  The Contractor shall include a clause in all subcontracts to require sub-contractors to comply with 
the safety provisions of this section as applicable.
8.1.3  The Contractor shall submit to the Contracting Officer and the Safety Coordinator a detailed safety 
program and continuous safety training plan which will be followed during the life of the Contract.  The 
Contractor will not deviate from the safety provisions of this section or make changes to the safety 
115 of 351

--- page 116 ---
program plan without prior review and approval by the Contracting Officer and the Safety Coordinator.
8.1.4  Contractor will ensure that an inspection of all shop areas is accomplished daily.  These 
inspections will be documented as to findings and corrective actions taken and monthly copies supplied 
to the Contracting Officer.
8.1.5 The Contractor will assign the Contract Manger to participate as a member of the City Service 
Center Safety Committee which meets monthly.
8.1.5 The Contractor will provide shop employees with weekly safety training on relevant training topics. 
Training documentation to be supplied to the Contracting Officer monthly.
8.1.6 The Contractor will ensure shop employees are properly trained/licensed to operate vehicles and 
equipment assigned for repair. This shall include Forklift, bucket truck, CDL’s and other license or 
certifications as applicable.
8.2  SPECIFIC REQUIREMENTS.
8.2.1  The Contractor shall load, handle, and transport City property in such a way as to prevent damage 
to the City property.
8.2.2  City property shall be stored in such a manner as to prevent damage to the City property.
8.2.2.1  Broken or damaged pallets shall not be used for storage of City property.
8.2.2.2  The Contractor shall provide sufficient aisles between storage areas for any material handling 
equipment that may be required.  Aisles shall be kept clean and dry at all times.
8.2.3  The Contractor shall inspect, maintain, and operate hoists, cranes, slings, and other lifting 
equipment in a safe manner to prevent damage to City property.
8.2.3.1
All lifting devices and equipment shall be visually inspected by the operator before 
each use or daily. On a periodic basis (annually) a documented inspection and weight 
test will be made on all hoists, cranes, slings, and other lifting equipment.  (IAW ANSI 
B30 Series Standards). Vehicles should not remain on lifts or lifting devices for 
extended periods of time or overnight.
8.2.3.2  Slings shall not be used when tied in knots or when damaged.
8.2.3.3  All jacks shall have a sufficient rating to lift and sustain the load.
8.2.4 The Contractor shall provide equipment specific training and certifications for equipment utilized 
by Contractor’s employees to include but not limited to – vehicle lifting devices, forklifts, aerial devices 
etc.
8.2.4  The Contractor shall maintain a workplace chemical list, maintain an OSHA Material Safety Data 
Sheet file, and advise and train his employees concerned of the chemical hazards to which they are 
exposed.  The informed handling and controlled disposal of hazardous and toxic materials shall be the 
responsibility of the Contractor.
Contract to supply a digital copy of these files to the City Fleet Manager on a quarterly basis, on City 
116 of 351

--- page 117 ---
request or upon Contractor changes to the file.
8.2.5  Flammable liquids in the vicinity of City property shall be handled and stored in a safe manner as 
per regulations to include: 
8.2.5.1  Precautions shall be taken to prevent the ignition of flammable vapors.
8.2.5.2  No smoking, spark producing equipment or open flames shall be permitted in any 
flammable liquid storage area.  (smoking is not permitted on any city property per city 
ordinance).
8.2.5.3 Proper handling of spills and approved disposal of waste material.
8.2.6  Spray applications using flammable and combustible materials in the vicinity of City property shall 
be done in accordance Cal OSHA  and the following:
8.2.6.1  All spray operations shall be done in a power ventilated spray booth or spray room.
8.2.6.2  All electrical service and electrical equipment within the spray booth or spray room shall 
be explosion proof.
8.2.6.3  No spark-producing equipment or open flames shall be permitted within ten feet of any 
opening in a spray booth or room.
8.2.6.4  Portable electric lamps shall not be used in any spray area during spray operations.
8.2.5 Proper PPE shall be worn by all personnel in the vicinity.
8.2.7  Compressed gas from cylinders in the vicinity of City property shall be handled and stored in 
accordance with Cal OSHA  and the following:
8.2.7.1  Compressed gas from cylinders shall not be used without reducing the pressure through a 
regulator.
8.2.7.2  When cylinders are not in use, the valve shall be closed tightly.
8.2.7.3  During use or storage, cylinders shall be restrained to prevent accidental upsetting or 
falling.
8.2.7.4  Smoking is not permitted on any city owned property.  "NO SMOKING" signs shall be 
posted.
8.2.7.5  Oxidizing gases shall not be stored within 50 feet of flammable liquids unless separated 
by a wall with one-hour fire rating.
8.2.7.6  All compressed gas cylinders shall be labeled as to contents.
8.2.7.7  Valve protector caps shall be installed on all compressed gas bottles in storage.
8.2.8  No smoking, spark producing equipment or open flames shall be allowed in the battery shop.
117 of 351

--- page 118 ---
8.2.9  Only qualified persons shall be authorized to perform welding operations and a qualified observer 
is to be deployed for the duration of welding operation.
8.2.10  Welding operations shall not be permitted where flammable materials, gases or liquids are 
present.
8.2.11  All precautions shall be taken during vehicle fueling to prevent the possibility of spillage, fire or 
explosions.
8.2.11.1  Vehicles shall not be fueled near open flames or spark producing devices.
8.2.11.2  Vehicles shall not be fueled indoors and personnel shall not smoke during fueling 
operations.
8.2.11.3  Vehicles being supplied with fuel shall have the ignition off and the parking brake 
applied.
8.2.11.4  During fueling, the nozzle of the fuel hose shall be kept in constant contact with the 
intake pipe of the vehicle's fuel tank.
8.2.11.5 Spilled fuel is to be handled in accordance with regulations and properly disposed.
8.2.11.6 EV Charging – Precautions shall be taken in the charging of EV vehicles. Any cords, 
connectors, ports or devices found to be out of compliance must be tagged out and the 
Contracting Officer notified.
8.2.11.7 EV Charging Cords- EV charging cords shall be placed in a manner as not to pose a 
tripping hazard. Upon completion of vehicle charging cords are to be properly stored on the 
Charging Device and the port placed in the assigned storage port.
8.2.12  Shop machinery will be inspected daily by shop personnel, and periodically maintained.
8.2.13 Shop machinery found to be out of compliance shall be locked out / tagged out and 
repairs scheduled. Contracting Officer to be notified.
8.2.13  Good housekeeping is essential to safe motor vehicle shop operations.
8.2.13.1  Shop floors will be kept clean and free of oil, grease, water, gasoline, or other hazardous 
and slippery materials.  Fuel and oil spills or other hazardous waste shall be promptly cleaned up 
and disposed of in an appropriate manner. Contractor to supply hazardous waste spill kits.
8.2.13.2  Drip pans under vehicles and mechanized equipment is essential.
8.2.13.3  Suitable containers with lids shall be strategically located throughout the work area for 
easy disposal of oil and grease soaked rags.  All containers for this purpose shall meet OSHA 
requirements and be UL listed.  Trash and oily rag receptacles shall be emptied daily.
8.2.13.3  Vehicle Storage Units left in the shop for extended periods or overnight shall be 
confirmed to be powered off or electrically isolated. Vehicles should not remain for extended 
periods or overnight on lifts or jackstands. Should the need arise, units remaining on a lift or 
118 of 351

--- page 119 ---
jackstands are to have secondary securement. Units without oil, or other vital fluids, waiting for 
parts or serious repair concerns are to have keys removed along with Out of Service tags, cones 
or steering wheel covers to ensure unit is not operated.  These items are to be supplied by the 
Contractor.
8.2.14  Shop personnel will wear appropriate personal protective equipment, to include but not limited 
to high visibility Jackets,  protective eyewear, gloves, bump/hardhats, slip resistant steel / composite toe 
boots, fall protection, as required when performing any hazardous maintenance operation.  PPE 
requirements will adhere to Cal OSHA Regulations and this equipment will be provided by the 
Contractor.
8.2.15  Chassis and axle supports will be used during vehicle maintenance.  No makeshift devices will be 
used for chassis and axle supports.
8.2.16  Tire Mounting.  Shop personnel will use mechanical devices, such as dollies, to help them mount 
or remove large, heavy tires.
8.2.16.1  Personnel will use guard cages when inflating heavy truck tires.
8.2.16.2  Personnel will use extreme caution when inflating tires or large trucks or heavy 
construction equipment.
8.2.17  Jacks.  The rated load will be legibly and permanently marked in a prominent location on the jack 
by casting, stamping, or other suitable means (jacks supplied with the vehicles as standard tool 
equipment are excluded).  The operator will make sure that the jack used has a rating sufficient to lift 
and sustain the load.  Jacks will be inspected, tested, and documented in compliance with ANSI B30.1 
American National Standard Safety Code for jacks, or an applicable technical order.  After a vehicle has 
been raised by a jack, it will be securely blocked to prevent falling.  At no time will a Technician place any 
part of their bodies directly under the wheels of a jacked vehicle.
8.2.18  Cables and Cords.  Power cables and cords on portable electrical equipment will be made of 
heavy armored rubber or similar material, to prevent damage from oil or grease, and by chafing.  Power 
cables and cords on all portable and fixed electrically operated equipment will be of the three-wire 
construction with a plug equipped with a ground lug.  (Note:  this requirement does not apply to double 
insulated tools.) Cables will be constructed to provide automatic grounding of equipment through 
integral conductors. Any cords or cables found to be worn or damaged must be removed from service 
and tagged out of service. Technicians utilizing portable electrical tools and lights will not string cables 
carelessly across shop floors.
8.2.19 Work area Isolation Areas where vehicle repair work is being performed, or vehicles are actively 
lifted or jacked shall have controlled access by means of cordoning off the area, closing of the garage 
door or safety chain across the garage door opening or other similar means. 
8.2.20 Roadside Safety   On the occasion of a roadside break down / repair, employees must have 
proper Cal OSHA approved PPE (such as High Visibility clothing etc.) additionally the work zone must be 
properly marked with safety triangles, flares and/or safety cones. Vehicle should be moved to the safest 
possible location for roadside service or vehicle recovery. Best practices to be applied. Local authorities 
to be notified as necessary and in a timely manner to ensure safety at the scene.
8.2.21  Fire Prevention.  The Contractor will follow all local fire laws, regulations, and standards to 
119 of 351

--- page 120 ---
ensure that damage does not occur to City property or personnel.
8.2.22 Ventilation  The Contractor will ensure proper ventilation of the shop area and avoid operating 
Internal Combustion Vehicles within the confines of the shop area. All safety measures shall be taken to 
avoid buildup of fumes, dust and airborne debris in the shop vicinity or into adjacent buildings.
SECTION 9
DEFINITIONS
91   Add On Oil  Oil added to a vehicle/equipment between oil changes.
9.2.  ASI (Annual Safety Inspection)  Maintenance performed annually; in accordance with state 
inspection requirements including LOF.
9.3   ASE  Automotive Service Excellence is an automotive institute that certifies automotive technicians 
in an array of automotive vocations, of these certifications ASE Master Technician is the pinnacle
9.4  BIT Biennial Inspection of Terminals A terminal Inspection with a requirement to inspect every 90 
days and maintain specific files for vehicles in excess of 10,000 lbs.
9.5  Captive Shop  A vehicle maintenance facility dedicated to the sole service of a single client’s fleet
9.6  CNG Compressed Natural Gas  A vehicle fuel that is comprised primarily of Methane and stored 
under pressure. Vehicles utilizing this fuel require specially certified technicians to maintain these 
systems.
9.6   Component  An individual part or piece of a larger system (i.e. Alternator, Starter, Fuel Pump)
9.7  Component Repair Limit.  The Component Repair Limit shall be $1,000.00 per component, per 
occurrence, per vehicle. All repair costs beyond this limit are the burden of the City and to be approved 
by the City Contracting Officer in advance of repair. Examples of typical Components are – Battery, 
Alternator, Water Pump, Catalytic Converter, Radiator, Brake Master Cylinder etc.  
Component Repair Limit will include diagnostics, labor (approved book time – Mitchel / ALLDATA etc.) 
component part, ancillary items and / or fluids.
Examples of a Typical Component repair: Failed Alternator- Alternator diag, R&R labor- Alternator (part) 
along with replacement of the alternator belt (ancillary) in this example: should a failed battery be 
found, the battery is a separate component, and not part of the Alternator Component Repair Limit. 
Bodywork in a single event shall be considered a single Component Repair with a limit of $1,000.00  
9.8   Contingency Operation.  Unanticipated increase or decrease of the level of service required.
9.9   Contractor.  A person or entity submitting a proposal under this RFP.
9.10  Contractor Assigned Vehicles.  City vehicles are defined as pooled vehicles which are operated and 
controlled primarily by Contractor personnel.
9.11  Contract Manager A person responsible for the performance of the work proposed under this RFP.
9.12  Contracting Officer.  A City person responsible for surveillance of Contractor performance.
120 of 351

--- page 121 ---
9.13  Contracting Officer Approval Authorization to proceed with a repair, accept charges or otherwise 
grant permission
9.14  Defective Service.  A unit of service which contains one or more defects, or nonconformance with 
specified requirements.
9.15  Delayed Maintenance.  Maintenance that can be delayed without damage to the 
vehicle/equipment or compromise safety standards or prevents the vehicle/equipment from being used 
for its designed function.
9.16  DTC Diagnostic Trouble Codes a system by which vehicle conditions are stored within the vehicle’s 
on-board computer 
9.17  Fleet Management Information System).  Computer Software utilized to provide computerized 
record of Fleet operations.
9.18  Joint Serviceability Inspection.  Inspection of vehicles, equipment, facilities by City and Contractor 
representation to inventory and determine their serviceability and physical condition.
9.19  Key Performance Indicator (KPI)  KPI’s are a metric utilized to evaluate performance and adherence 
to contract requirements.
9.20  LOF (Lube, Oil and Filter).  Maintenance performed periodically as specified by the manufacturer
9.21  Major Repair.  Repair that is generally done in fixed workshops.  It includes, but is not limited to, 
the following type of work:  (1) repairing and replacing parts, assemblies, subassemblies and 
components; (2) fabrication of parts, when required (weld, lathe work, etc.) (3) body and structural 
repairs; (4) painting; (5) upholstery repairs; (6) scheduled inspections; (7) modification; and (8) corrosion 
control.
9.22   Minor Repair.  Minor repair is the changing of parts such as mirrors, radiator and gas caps, 
windshield wiper arms and blades, fuses, lightbulbs, fan belts, etc.  This includes minor adjustments that 
can be finished in one half hour or less.  These repairs can be completed in or by the diagnostic and 
quality assurance section, general purpose repair shop, or any combination of them.  As a rule, the 
operator stays with the vehicle while these repairs are done.
9.23   Monitoring.  Those actions taken by a Contractor to control the performance of services so that 
they meet the requirements of the Scope of Work section.
9.24   On Board Data Vehicle information stored with in a vehicle’s on-board computer. Typical Data 
may include Diagnostic Trouble Codes, vehicle mileage, fuel level and battery state of charge.
9.25   Operational Contract Start Date.  The date the Contractor assumes all responsibility for vehicle 
maintenance in accordance with the Scope of Work section.
9.26   Original Equipment Manufacturer.  The manufacturer of the complete production vehicle, 
commercial or military, whether assembled from parts of its own manufacture or from parts or 
components furnished by other manufacturers or a combination of both.
9.27   Original Parts Manufacturer.  A manufacturer of automotive parts supplied direct to the original 
121 of 351

--- page 122 ---
equipment manufacturer for incorporation into the production vehicle and/or resale as replacement 
parts.  The original equipment manufacturer is the actual parts manufacturer for those parts produced 
solely by it.
9.28   Out of Contract Costs  Costs for maintenance, diagnostics, repair or installation that fall outside 
the scope of the contract.
9.29  Performance Requirement Indicator  The maximum limit of acceptable downtime that is 
established per fleet vehicle classification. 
9.30  Personal Protective Equipment. Personal protective equipment, commonly referred to as "PPE", is 
equipment worn to minimize exposure to hazards that cause serious workplace injuries and illnesses.
9.31  Priority Repair.  Repair required of emergency vehicles or other vehicles when further loss of 
vehicles will degrade mission support.
9.32  Quality Assurance.  Those actions taken by the City to assure services meet the requirements in the 
Scope of Work Section.
9.33  Rebuilt / Remanufactured Parts.  Used parts that have been dismantled and reconstructed as 
necessary; all internal and external parts are cleaned and free from rust and corrosion; all impaired, 
defective, or substantially worn parts are restored to a sound condition or replaced with new, rebuilt, or 
unimpaired used parts; all missing parts are replaced with new, rebuilt, or unimpaired used parts; and 
such other operations are performed as necessary to put the product in sound working condition.  Must 
meet or exceed original manufacturer's specification.
9.34  Recalibration A process by which a system is reset or calibrated to new or updated conditions 
9.35  Special Marking.  Any marking authorized of special significance to a particular user essential to 
effective communication within that unit.
9.36  Telematics  A system by which vehicle on board data may be recorded and transmitted.
9.37  TPMS Tire Pressure Monitoring System A system that can alert a driver to an under inflated tire
9.38   Vehicle.  An item of equipment mounted on wheels, tracks, runners, rollers or any combination of 
them which is designed for highway and/or land operation which derive power from a self-contained 
power unit or is designed to be towed by and/or used in conjunction with such        self-propelled 
equipment.
9.39  Vehicle Accessory and Special Equipment.  An item added to a vehicle to meet an operational 
requirement.  The item shall be transferred from one vehicle and installed on another vehicle when 
authorized by the Contracting Officer.  Examples of accessory and special equipment are spotlights, 
spare tire racks, mirrors, horns, coolant/oil/battery heaters, lights, campers, cargo shells, hydraulic tail 
gates, tow hitches, winches, etc.
9.40  VDP (Vehicle Deadlined for Parts).  A vehicle placed in an out of commission status due to the 
nonavailability of parts.
9.41   VDP (Vehicle Deadlined for Repair)  A vehicle placed in an out of commission status for repair
122 of 351

--- page 123 ---
9.42  VOC (Vehicle Out of Commission) The total time a vehicle is out of commission for repair and parts 
(VDR plus VDP).
SECTION 10
PERFORMANCE REQUIREMENTS INDICATORS
10.0  GENERAL The City intends to establish performance standards and utilize specific Key Point 
Indicators (KPI’s)  to monitor Contractor performance. These KPI’s may include Safety, Regulatory 
Compliance,  Technician Certification Compliance, Staffing, Fleet Availability, Vehicle Down Time, PM 
Currency, Shop productivity, rebound / rework statistics, and other metrics the City deems relevant to 
performance under this agreement.  These standards will factor as “Key Performance Indicators” in 
correlation with “Performance Based Compensation” award
10.0.1 FLEET PERFORMANCE STANDARDS:
Performance standards have been established for each class of vehicle or equipment based on 
availability.  Availability will be calculated by multiplying the number of units X hour basis X 30 days.  The 
results will be multiplied by the percentage of acceptable downtime in order to establish the allowable 
hours of downtime.  Exceeding the allowable downtime limits will cause the deduction to be made from 
the next monthly payment.
10.0.2   Downtime Calculation: Downtime shall start at the time the vehicle or equipment is delivered to 
the Contractor for service.  “Requests for Services slips” will be date and timed stamped at the time the 
vehicle is left for service. 
10.0.3  Acceptable levels of down time and deductions:  The following downtimes are acceptable for 
each Class.  The percentage deduction will be made from the monthly flat fee should the downtime 
limits be exceeded.

10.0.4  No single vehicle or piece of equipment shall be out of service for more than seven calendar 
days.  After this period, should the City need to rent a substitute vehicle or piece of equipment, the 
Contractor shall reimburse the City for the resulting rental charges.  Contractor may petition the 
contracting officer to exonerate payment of rental costs when documented evidence demonstrates the 
repair was impossible due to conditions outside the Contractor’s control.

Alex Khojikian, City Manager

Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
May 19, 2025 
SUBJECT:
Wastewater Treatment Plant, Digester 2 Coating Project – Agreement Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an Agreement with Brand Safway to conduct Wastewater Treatment Plant Digester 2 Coatings in an amount not 
to exceed $406,881.35; approve a contingency of $82,000.00; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the 
agreement in substantially the form presented and approve any necessary change orders within the approved contingency 
amount. 
BACKGROUND:
The Clean Water Program (CWP) Annual Major Components (AMC) Projects includes several capital improvement projects 
that are currently under development or under construction and are intended to upgrade or rehabilitate aging 
infrastructure in the City’s sewer collection system and Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP). The AMC includes the 
WWTP Biogas and Biosolids Evaluation project which is being conducted by Brown and Caldwell (B&C). The scope includes 
the condition assessment and inspection of both digesters. An initial condition assessment of Digester 2 was recently 
completed and revealed that the coatings of the draft tube and interior of Digester 2 need repair. This will help prevent 
wear and tear related issues caused by the composition of digester sludge and gas. 
Digester 2 is currently offline due to the mixer failure in 2022, which is being repaired off site and expected back in late 
May 2025. The WWTP is currently operating with only Digester 1, which is the older of the two Digesters, and there is 
concern about its current condition. It is in the City’s best interest to bring Digester 2 online as soon as possible. Operating 
the plant with only Digester 1 causes an increase in the liquid content in the off-haul material. This has increased the 
operational cost of hauling the material by $26,000 per month. 
With Digester 2 offline, the City performed a cleaning and condition assessment of Digester 2 in the second week of 
March. To perform the condition assessment, an internal temporary scaffold was installed. Because the digester is egg 
shaped, the scaffold is complex and is costly to install. After the inspection and preliminary evaluation was performed, it 
was recommended to re-coat the digester and draft tube because the existing coating has worn off. Without the coating, 
the interior of the digester would be subject to corrosion which can cause issues with Digester 2 condition and 
performance. Given the results of this evaluation, the City deems it is most cost effective to re-coat the interior of the 
digester and draft tube while Digester 2 is currently offline, and the scaffolding is in place. This avoids the costs of 
dismantling and installing the scaffolding and recleaning the digester if the recoating is not performed while the digester is 
currently offline. In addition, taking a digester offline is not a simple process as it involves ensuring the gases are purged, 
which takes significant effort from the WWTP operations and maintenance staff. 
In April 2025, the City obtained three proposals from three local coating vendors – JeffCo, Brand Safway (which owns 
National Coatings), and Redwood. City staff evaluated the proposals and determined Brand Safway as the lowest bidder to 
135 of 351

--- page 136 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
perform the work. They also demonstrated experience with this scope. The base amount for this project is $406,881.35, 
which includes labor, material, coating per manufacturer specifications, decontamination, dehumidification, and onsite 
power. In addition, staff recommends $82,000 be authorized as a contingency amount for any potential changes that may 
arise due to the nature of this work. The approximate duration of this work is 27 working days. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There are sufficient funds available in the CWP WWTP Annual Major Components Project (46T090) to fund this agreement 
and the proposed contingency reserve. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, 
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 
15301.)

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Internal Coatings
•
Perform CSN testing Chlor-Rid wash the interior surfaces. Wash the interior surfaces utilizing 
Clor-Rid to remove soluble salts. One wash included.
•
Abrasive blast the shell surfaces of the egg-shaped digester to an SSPC-SP10 Near White Metal 
Blast Cleaning, with a minimum anchor profile of the 2-4 mils. Estimated at 17,850 FT2. Garnet 
abrasive to be utilized for this step to avoid any abrasive embedment.
•
Apply a stripe coat of Dura-Plate 8200, per the manufacturer’s instructions, to all weld seams 
that coat. 
•
Apply 1 coat of Dura-Plate 8200, per the manufacturer’s instructions at 20-35 mils DFT.
•
High voltage spark test the coated surfaces per NACE-SP0188.
•
Take DFT Readings per SSPC-PA2 Method no. 2.
o
Abrasive blast the interior of the draft tube according to NAPF 500-03.
o
Wash the interior surfaces of the draft tube with Chlor-Rid to remove soluble salts. One 
wash included.
o
Apply 1 coat of Dura-Plate 8200, per the manufacturer’s instructions at a minimum of 20 
mils DFT.
o
DFT and Holiday test accessible areas.
Exclusions/Clarifications
•
Any worked performed outside the work stated within, will be considered extra work.
•
Any delays or call outs will be considered extra work.
•
No training time for site access has been included.
•
No disposal or handling of hazardous waste has been included.
•
Air monitoring or sampling.
•
1 Chlor-Rid wash has been included in this pricing.
•
This quote was based on interior access being supplied by others.
•
No containment included other than ground coverage.

SUBJECT:
East San Mateo Sanitary Sewer Lift Station Rehabilitation Project – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 6 with Schaaf & Wheeler for professional design services for the East San Mateo Sanitary Sewer 
Lift Station Rehabilitation Project to provide engineering services during construction in an amount not to exceed 
$334,247, for a total agreement amount of $2,396,431; amend the Scope of Project; extend the term; and authorize the 
Public Works Director to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented and issue amendments within the 
balance of the previously approved contingency.
BACKGROUND:
The Clean Water Program is improving the City's sanitary sewer system to prevent sanitary sewer overflows and 
unauthorized discharge of sewage. In 2016, a Sewer Pump Station and Force Main Condition Assessment (Assessment) 
was completed by AECOM, building on a previous pump station capacity study to improve the City’s lift stations’ reliability. 
The East San Mateo Lift Station Rehabilitation Project (Project) addresses multiple lift stations, including the five highest 
priority lift stations from the Assessment: Kelly/Kehoe, Laurie Meadows, and Los Prados Nos. 1, 2, and 3. 
On February 24, 2017, City Council awarded a professional design services agreement to Schaaf & Wheeler for this Project. 
The Project was split into two packages for efficient delivery. Staff coordinated with Schaaf & Wheeler to complete each 
package with a three-phase approach: 1) alternatives analysis, 2) detailed design, and 3) engineering services during 
construction. 
Package 1 included the abandonment of the Laurie Meadows lift station, the upgrade of the Woodbridge lift station, and 
the modifications to the surrounding sewers to redirect sewer flows. The scope of the original agreement included an 
alternatives analysis for these improvements. Three amendments were sequentially approved to allow Schaaf & Wheeler 
to progress through the Package 1 design and construction phases: Amendment No. 1 included scope for detailed design, 
Amendment No. 2 included additional investigations required to progress the design, and Amendment No. 3 included 
engineering services during construction. The construction contract was awarded to JMB Construction in 2019 and the 
project was completed in 2020. 
Package 2 originally included the rehabilitation of the Los Prados area lift stations and Kelly/Kehoe lift station. In 2021, 
staff determined that the Arroyo lift station also required improvements. Utilizing Schaaf & Wheeler’s existing contract 
balance, Amendment No. 4 increased their scope to perform an alternatives analysis of these lift stations. The alternatives 
analysis recommendations for the Package 2 improvements include the Los Prados No. 1 lift station replacement and force 
main extension, the elimination of Los Prados No. 2 lift station, sewer main improvements between Los Prados No. 1 and 
No. 2 lift stations, Kelly/Kehoe lift station replacement and force main extension, and the Arroyo lift station rehabilitation. 
Amendment No. 5 increased budget and scope for Schaaf & Wheeler to provide detailed design phase services for the 
147 of 351

--- page 148 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
recommended Package 2 improvements. 
As part of the Package 2 scope, this Amendment No. 6 will maintain Schaaf & Wheeler’s engineering services during 
construction from construction award through construction completion. Staff reviewed and negotiated a proposal with 
Schaaf & Wheeler for Amendment No. 6 for a not-to-exceed amount of $334,247. Staff determined the proposal is 
reasonable for the scope of work and expertise required and recommend approving Amendment No. 6 to the agreement.
City Council previously approved a contingency reserve, which has a remaining balance of $87,200. An additional 
contingency request is not requested with the proposed amendment as this balance is anticipated to be sufficient to 
address unknowns and risks that may impact Schaaf & Wheeler’s scope and fee through the duration of the construction 
contract.

ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The work addressed by this administrative report is being undertaken to support the Clean Water Program. This project is 
subject to the requirements of the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA), the general components of which are 
included as part of the Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) (SCH No. 201532006) that was 
prepared for the Clean Water Program. The Final PEIR was certified by City Council on June 6, 2016. The City prepared 
Addenda to the Final PEIR that was approved on July 16, 2018 (Addendum 1) and April 15, 2019 (Addendum 2). This work 
is within the scope of the Project evaluated in the PEIR and Addendum.

WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo (“City”), a municipal corporation of the State 
of California, and Schaaf & Wheeler (“CONSULTANT”), entered into an Agreement for 
professional services (“Agreement”) on February 15, 2017; and 
 
WHEREAS, on July 24, 2017, the CITY and CONSULTANT executed 
Amendment No. 1, extending the scope of the Agreement, the term of the Agreement, 
and increasing Agreement amount by $723,327, for a total Agreement in the amount of 
$1,037,448; and 
 
 
WHEREAS, on October 17, 2017, the CITY and CONSULTANT executed 
Amendment No. 2, extending the scope of the Agreement without additional funds, 
maintaining the Agreement amount at $1,037,448; and 
 
WHEREAS, on October 7, 2019, the CITY and CONSULTANT executed 
Amendment No. 3, extending the scope of the Agreement, the term of the Agreement, 
and increasing the Agreement amount by $153,312, for a total Agreement in the amount 
of $1,190,760; and 
 
 
WHEREAS, on May 10, 2021, the CITY and CONSULTANT executed 
Amendment No. 4, extending the scope of the Agreement without additional funds, 
maintaining the Agreement amount of $1,190,760; and 
 
WHEREAS, on April 7, 2022, the CITY and CONSULTANT executed 
Amendment No. 5, extending the scope of the Agreement, the term of the Agreement, 
and increasing the Agreement amount by $871,424, for a total Agreement in the amount 
of $2,062,184; and 
 
 
WHEREAS, City and Consultant, wish to amend the Agreement to include 
Services During Construction as described in the attached Scope of Work. Amendment 6 
amends the Agreement to amend the Scope of Work, increase the Agreement amount by 
$334,237, for a new total of $2,396,421, and extend the term of the Agreement.

SCOPE OF SERVICES 
As part of the East San Mateo Lift Station Rehabilitation Project, the Consultant will provide 
additional engineering consulting services for the following items which have been identified by 
the City’s Clean Water Program (CWP): 
1. Provide additional General Services (Task 1) for the extended contract duration and 
additional construction contract.   
2. Provide construction phase services for the Los Prados, Kehoe Kelly, and Arroyo Lift 
Station Rehabilitation Project, City Project No. 469988. 
 
TASK 1 – General Services 
Additional general services will be performed by the Consultant throughout the project as 
necessary for the extended contract duration and additional construction contract.  These services 
include:   
Task 1.1 – Project Management 
Task 1.1.1 – General Management 
The Consultant will be responsible for detailed management of the project, including 
subconsultants and subcontractors, and will keep the City appraised of the status of the project. 
The Consultant will provide the key management personnel as described in their proposal on this 
project. The Consultant will not reassign the key project personnel without prior approval of the 
City per the Standard Agreement for Professional Consultant Services. 
Task 1.1.4 – Progress Report 
The Consultant will prepare and submit monthly progress reports that include a narrative of the 
work completed by task, project decision log, project action item log, upcoming work, project 
issues, budget and schedule status, percent complete, cost to complete, earned value versus 
actual spent analysis, potential scope or budget changes, and other important project information. 
Task 1.1.5 – Project Invoices 
The Consultant will prepare and submit monthly invoices in accordance with Program standards. 
The invoices will document the man-hours and billing rates for staff for each task in the WBS, as 
well as overhead, profit and any direct costs. The current and previous billing period invoicing, as 
well as a summary of the budget spent, budget remaining, cost to complete, and all backup 
documentation for expenses will be included. The monthly progress report and project schedule 
will be submitted with the project invoice as part of the monthly request for payment. 
Task 1.1.7 – Progress Schedule 
The Consultant will prepare a cost loaded project schedule in significant detail to calculate a 
monthly earned value of work performed. The selection of tasks and task durations will be 
approved by the City. The Consultant will prepare a planned value curve for the Project. Prior to 
invoice submittal, the Consultant will evaluate the percent complete for each activity worked on 
during the billing period. The Consultant will calculate the earned value for the month. The earned 
value will be compared to the planned value and the actual invoice value for the month. The

Consultant will need to justify any requests for monies over the planned value and explain how

Task 1.5 – Management of Subconsultants  
If the Consultant requires the services of any subconsultants, then the Consultant will include a 
list of them in the proposal, explain why they are needed, and provide a general description of 
their effort. 
The Consultant will manage the activities of subconsultants during performance of the project. All 
requirements of the contract shall also apply to subconsultants. 
Task 7 –Construction Phase Services 
It is assumed that all work designed as part of the Los Prados, Kehoe Kelly, and Arroyo Lift 
Station Rehabilitation Project will be constructed under one construction contract. 
The Consultant shall provide services during construction, which may include the following:  
 
Attendance at pre-construction conference.  Agenda and minutes for meetings will be 
prepared by others. 
 
Attendance at construction progress meetings via teleconference meeting (assume 1 
hour each and 80 meetings in total) by one Consultant representative, additional 
meeting attendance can be provided for an additional fee upon request). Agenda and 
minutes for meetings will be prepared by others. 
o Electrical engineer will attend up to 4 meetings 
 
Project correspondence and general technical support including email and telephone 
correspondence throughout the duration of construction.   
 
Periodic field visits (assumed 12 field visits by Schaaf & Wheeler staff) 
o Scope includes up to 4 field visits by the project geotechnical engineer to review 
existing conditions and provide recommendations to engineering staff.  This does 
not include material testing or inspection services.  
 
General technical support 
 
Submittal review 
 
Request for information review 
 
Change order and contract document modifications preparation and review 
 
Startup and commissioning support  (assumed 3 field visits) 
o Assume up to three site visits for final walk through (one per lift station) and 
preparation of punch list 
 
Construction closeout support 
 
Preparation of record drawings 
 
Preparation of O&M manuals 
 
Review of warranty documents 
 
Attendance at a post-construction team meeting 
Task 8 – Environmental Permit Compliance 
Schaaf & Wheeler’s subconsultant, WRA, Inc., will provide environmental permit compliance 
support services as described below: 
 
Preconstruction Surveys and Reporting

Attachment A5, Scope of Services - Sanitary Sewer Pump Station Rehabilitation Design Services 
Amendment 6 
 
 
Page 4 of 4 
o Coordinate with CDFW to approve qualified Biologists and Biological Monitors 
o Two early detection surveys to identify active bird nests, bat roosts, or woodrat 
nests.  Results will be transmitted via email, no formal reporting is required.   
o Woodrat nest survey (as required by the SAA) - If woodrat nests are found in the 
work area, additional consultation services may be necessary which are not 
covered under this scope.  
o 48-Hours pre-construction survey (as required by the SAA) - If nesting birds or 
roosting bats are found in the work area, additional consultation services may be 
necessary which are not covered under this scope. 
 
Daily Inspections (as required by the SAA) – A qualified Biologist or Biological Monitor 
will conduct daily inspections, consisting of a maximum of 1 inspection per day.  This 
scope of work covers up to 40 daily inspections.  This task assumes that no special-
status species will be present and therefore no formal reporting will be necessary.  If the 
construction schedule requires additional daily inspections, additional budget will be 
necessary.  
 
Revegetation Plan Monitoring and Reporting (5 Years) 
o Complete monitoring and reporting requirements defined in Section 5 of the 
Revegetation Plan.  
o Prepare annual report with photo documentation points and a map figure per the 
NOA requirements.  
o This scope includes 5 surveys and 5 annual reports. If the final success criteria 
are not achieved, additional budget may be necessary for reporting in 
subsequent years.   
 
RWQCB Notice of Termination – Prepare and submit RWQCB Notice of Termination 
Report.  
 
Project Management and Coordination – Coordination with City, CDFW, and RWQCB.  
This scope includes up to 30 hours of coordination by WRA staff.  
Task 9 – Prepare Standard Operating Procedures 
Schaaf & Wheeler will prepare standard operating procures for each of the three lift stations.  
The procedures will include the following: 
 
Standard heath and safety warnings  
 
General description of the pump station and surrounding sewer system 
 
Operating procedure 
 
Pump station setpoints  
 
Station controls and control strategy  
 
Power failure and standby generator description  
It is assumed that the standard operating procedure will be similar to the Standard Operating 
Procedure for DAPS Interim Operation – December 2021.

SUBJECT:
On-Call Professional Consultant Services Agreement – Amendment Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 3 to the agreement with Sanbell-Bay Area, formerly Bellecci & Associates, for on-call 
professional design services increasing the agreement amount by $200,000, for a new agreement total of $450,000; 
extending the term of the Agreement to June 30, 2027; and authorizing the Director of Public Works to execute 
amendments within the Agreement amount including no-cost extensions.
BACKGROUND:
In October 2018, Public Works staff issued a Request for Proposals (RFP) to select qualified firms to provide on-call 
professional consulting services. The City received proposals from thirteen (13) firms and evaluated them based on project 
understanding, relevant experience, project manager qualifications, and technical capabilities. Three firms were 
shortlisted, and in-person interviews were conducted with each project team. Sanbell-Bay Area (Sanbell), formerly Bellecci 
& Associates, Inc., was among the three firms selected to provide engineering support under an original agreement of 
$250,000. 
In January 2024, Sanbell was engaged to provide engineering design services in support of San Mateo's implementation of 
a Train Quiet Zone. The scope of work included general project management and coordination, development of conceptual 
and final designs, and right-of-way mapping. 
In Summer 2024, staff and Sanbell presented conceptual designs to City Council, which included a closure at Villa Terrace 
and median improvements at East Bellevue Avenue. Due to potential long-term impacts on surrounding residents, 
particularly related to loss of parking locations, the Council directed staff to further evaluate the project design at East 
Bellevue Avenue and to incorporate additional traffic operational analysis along previously unstudied intersections on 
Claremont Street. 
Staff has been working with Sanbell to implement the necessary design changes and expand outreach efforts within the 
existing budget. However, additional funds are now required to meet Council expectations and to address newly expanded 
project scope elements. 
Additional project elements requiring expanded scope and funding for Sanbell include: 
1.
Additional design services for storm drain improvements at Villa Terrace 
2.
Expanded right-of-way services and boundary research for Caltrain and Union Pacific rights-of-way
3.
Revisions to design documents to potentially account for both complete and temporary closures 
4.
Additional coordination with agencies such as CPUC, Caltrain, Caltrans, and Union Pacific 
5.
Bid and construction support services 
159 of 351

--- page 160 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
The expected cost for these additional tasks is conservatively estimated at $200,000 but will be refined further with 
Sanbell prior to issuance of Task Orders. 
The City Council previously authorized amendments to Sanbell’s contract on March 21, 2022, and June 5, 2023, extending 
the contract term through December 31, 2025, without increasing the project budget. Given Sanbell’s ongoing 
involvement and expertise in the Train Quiet Zone efforts, as well as their responsiveness to City requests, staff 
recommends amending their existing on-call contract to provide additional design and consulting services in the amount 
not-to-exceed of $200,000, for a total agreement amount of $450,000, and extend the term through June 30, 2027, 
beyond the anticipated implementation date of December 2026. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There are sufficient funds in the Train Quiet Zone Project (462205) to fund this Amendment No. 3. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This amendment is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not 
result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)  In addition, the 
proposed work relating to the Villa Terrace closure and median improvements at East Bellevue Avenue will include 
separate CEQA review documentation prepared for the project.
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SUBJECT:
2025 Annual Investment Policy – Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution approving the City of San Mateo 2025 Investment Policy and authorizing investments in United States 
Treasury obligations, Federal Agency obligations and State and Local Municipal obligations with a maximum maturity of up 
to seven years and an aggregate amount not to exceed ten percent of the City’s investment portfolio at the time of 
purchase.
BACKGROUND:
The investment of public funds by a California local agency, including the types of securities in which an agency may invest, 
is governed by the California Government Code Sections 53000-53610. The City’s Investment Policy provides a framework 
for managing public funds with a focus on safety, liquidity and return, and is designed to comply with State law and best 
practices in public fund management.
The City’s investment policy is reviewed periodically to reflect changes in investment strategies and regulatory updates. It 
has been the City’s practice to bring the investment policy to the City Council annually for review and approval, regardless 
of whether changes are proposed.
The current policy is more conservative than State law, including a more limited list of eligible investments and stricter 
caps on investment types and durations. Notably, the City currently limits the maximum maturity for all fixed-income 
securities to five (5) years, even though State law permits longer maturities under certain conditions.
As part of the 2025 annual review, staff identified an opportunity to update the Investment Policy to allow longer 
maturities, up to seven (7) years, for a limited set of high-quality fixed-income securities: 
•
United States Treasury obligations
•
United States Federal Agency obligations
•
State and Local Municipal obligations
This proposed change is timely and strategic for the following reasons:
Interest Rate Environment Creates a Unique Opportunity
The current fixed-income investment environment reflects a historically high-interest rate cycle. The yield curve, 
previously inverted, has flattened with some upward movement in long-term yields. While rates have declined slightly 
from recent peaks, they remain attractive.  Allowing certain high-quality investments to extend to seven (7) years would 
enable the City to lock in attractive long-term rates, supporting consistent interest earnings over time.
163 of 351

--- page 164 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
As shown below in Table 1, a 7-year U.S. Treasury currently yield 4.1 percent, compared to 3.9 percent for a 5-year or 3.8 
percent for a 3-year.  
These yields exceed the current core inflation rate, which remains around 3.0 percent per the latest CPI information. The 
ability to invest at the longer end of the yield curve allows the City to protect purchasing power and generate consistent 
income while maintaining a high level of safety and credit quality.
Table 1: Treasury market rates as of May 2, 2025 *
Treasury Notes
Market Yield
7-Year Note
4.107%
5-Year Note
3.920%
3-Year Note
3.813%
2-Year Note
3.832%
1-Year Note
4.002%
              *Note: It is important to note that interest rates fluctuate daily and are unlikely to match exactly the rates shown in Table 1.
Alignment with the City's Investment Approach: The City does not invest in equities. Instead, our investment portfolio is 
composed of high-quality fixed-income securities, structured to prioritize safety and long-term stability.  Investments in 
the longer-term portfolio are typically held to maturity.  Expanding the allowable maturity for certain high-quality 
securities aligns with this conservative approach and enhances both portfolio diversification and income stability.
Limited to High-Quality Securities: The proposed change applies only to the most secure investment types:  U.S. Treasury 
obligations (backed by the full faith and credit of the federal government), U.S. Federal Agency obligations, and State and 
Local Municipal obligations. 
Portfolio Diversification with Risk Control: The proposed change includes a 10 percent cap on securities with maturities 
beyond five years. This ensures that while the City can take advantage of higher long-term yields, the overall portfolio 
duration remains balanced, and risk exposure is managed within acceptable limits.
Support Fund Reserve Structure: All major City funds, including the General Fund, Special Revenue Funds, Enterprise 
Funds, and Internal Service Funds, maintain long-term reserves. Investing a portion of these reserves in longer-duration, 
high-quality securities is financially prudent and aligned with the long-term nature of the City’s reserve structure.
Next Steps
Under Government Code Section 53601, investments with maturities beyond five years require the City Council to grant 
express authority to make the investment either specifically or as part of an investment program. If the proposed 
Resolution and Amendments to the Investment Policy are approved by the City Council, the City will be authorized to 
purchase longer term securities as part of its investment program after a 90-day (three-month) waiting period.  
BUDGET IMPACT:
Approval of the proposed changes to the City's Investment Policy for 2025 will not have an immediate budgetary impact.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
Approval of the City’s 2025 Investment Policy is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is a government fiscal activity 
which does not involve any commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially significant physical impact 
on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
RESOLUTION NO. ________  (2025)
ADOPTING THE INVESTMENT POLICY FOR THE CITY OF SAN MATEO 
AND AUTHORIZING INVESTMENTS IN UNITED STATES TREASURY OBLIGATIONS, 
UNITED STATES FEDERAL AGENCY OBLIGATIONS, AND STATE AND LOCAL MUNICIPAL 
OBLICAITONS WITH A MAXIMUM MATURITY UP TO SEVEN YEARS AND AN AGGREGATE 
AMOUNT NOT TO EXCEED TEN PERCENT OF THE CITY’S INVESTMENT PORTFOLIO AT THE 
TIME OF PURCHASE
WHEREAS, investment policies guide staff and their advisors for all investment activities on 
behalf of cities; and
WHEREAS, those investment activities are primarily governed by the individual city’s adopted 
investment policies and by California state law (Government Code sections 53600-53610); and
WHEREAS, the Investment Policy for the City of San Mateo is consistent with state law and, for 
the purpose of added safety and liquidity, is more restrictive than state law; and
WHEREAS, Government Code section 53646 requires annual review and approval of a city’s 
investment policy only if there are changes, however it encourages cities to conduct an annual review 
and approval process even if there are no proposed changes; and
WHEREAS, recognizing the importance of the City’s Investment Policy, it is the City’s practice to 
bring the investment policy to the City Council annually for review and approval regardless of whether 
there are proposed changes; and
WHEREAS, Government Code Section 53601 limits investments with maturities beyond five 
years unless express authority is granted by the governing body either for a specific investment or as 
part of an investment program; and
WHEREAS, based on the current market environment and long-term reserve structure of City 
funds, staff recommends extending the maximum maturity from five years to seven years for specific 
high-quality fixed-income securities, in order to better align with the City’s long-term reserve structure 
and investment strategy; and
WHEREAS, the proposed amendments to the Investment Policy authorize such longer-term 
investments only in the following three categories: United States Treasury obligations, United States 
Federal Agency obligations, and State and Local Municipal obligations; and
WHEREAS, the proposed amendment also establishes that the aggregate amount of 
investments beyond five years shall not exceed ten percent (10%) of the total City investment portfolio 
at the time of purchase. 
NOW, THEREFORE, THE SAN MATEO CITY COUNCIL HEREBY RESOLVES that:

extend the maximum maturity for certain securities from five (5) years to seven (7) years,
